Blue Owl caps fund redemptions after $5.4B in withdrawal requests

Blue Owl Capital disclosed on Thursday that it will limit redemptions to 5% at two of its private credit funds after investors sought to pull an unprecedented share of their money during the first quarter, marking the most severe test yet of the embattled private credit sector's ability to manage a wave of investor exits.

Published
51 minutes ago
investing
Blue Owl shares sink 9% as redemption requests hit 40% in tech fund
cnbc
Blue Owl private credit funds redemptions capped at 5% after steep ...
marketscreener
Blue Owl limits withdrawals in two funds after historic surge in ...
ft
Blue Owl struck by $5.4bn of redemption requests - Financial Times
cnbc.com
A Rush for the Exits

Investors in Blue Owl's technology-focused fund, Owl Technology Income Corp (OTIC), submitted redemption requests totaling 40.7% of outstanding shares, while its larger Blue Owl Credit Income Corp (OCIC) fund received requests amounting to 21.9%, according to shareholder letters released Thursday. Together, the requests totaled roughly $5.4 billion, according to the Financial Times.
investing
+2

Both funds will honor only the standard 5% quarterly repurchase cap on a pro rata basis. OCIC's portfolio was valued at $36 billion as of December 31, 2025, diversified across 370 companies and 31 industries, while OTIC held $6.2 billion in fair value across 190 companies.
marketscreener
+2

Blue Owl attributed the surge to "increased market apprehensions regarding AI-related disruptions impacting software companies" and what it called a "meaningful disconnect" between public sentiment on private credit and the underlying performance of its portfolios. In OCIC, approximately 90% of the fund's 90,000 shareholders chose not to tender their shares, with just 1% of shareholders accounting for the majority of requests.
cnbc
+2

4 sources
Contagion Across Private Credit

The disclosure sent Blue Owl shares sharply lower on Thursday and weighed on the broader alternative asset management sector. Blue Owl's redemption figures dwarf those reported by peers earlier this quarter: Ares Management capped withdrawals at its $10.7 billion fund after clients sought to redeem 11.6%, Apollo Global Management imposed the same cap at its $15.1 billion Apollo Debt Solutions fund following 11.2% in requests, and BlackRock-owned HPS restricted redemptions for the first time after requests hit 9.3% of its $26 billion fund.
withintelligence
+4

The pattern of gated withdrawals across the industry has left more than $4.6 billion of investor capital trapped behind redemption limits this quarter, according to Bloomberg estimates, with roughly $13 billion in total requests submitted across more than a dozen funds.
bloomberg

6 sources
A Sector Under Pressure

Thursday's news is the latest chapter in a months-long crisis of confidence in the $1.8 trillion private credit market. In February, Blue Owl permanently halted redemptions at its OBDC II fund and sold $1.4 billion in loan assets at 99.7% of par value to pension and insurance investors. That move, along with questions raised by investment firm Glendon Capital Management about whether Blue Owl and peers were understating portfolio losses, triggered a broader selloff in alternative asset manager stocks that has erased more than $265 billion in market capitalization since last year's peaks.
reuters
+4

Despite the scale of the requests, Blue Owl noted that actual net outflows remained modest: OCIC saw net outflows of $116 million, less than 1% of net asset value, after accounting for $872 million in gross capital inflows, while OTIC's net outflows were $52 million.
investing

UBS freezes real estate fund withdrawals for up to 3 years

UBS has suspended redemptions from its Germany-based Euroinvest real estate fund for up to three years, citing insufficient liquidity to meet a surge in withdrawal requests, according to an investor notice seen by Reuters.
marketscreener

The fund had assets under management of €406.8 million ($469.4 million) at the end of February, according to a fund fact sheet. In the notice, UBS said any redemption requests submitted after March 25 would not be executed. The bank also suspended the issuance of new shares, warning that additional sales were unlikely to improve fund liquidity and could expose new investors to heightened risks if the fund is ultimately wound up.
marketscreener

"In this challenging market environment, UBS Real Estate GmbH has taken the decision to suspend redemptions at this time to ensure the protection of all our investors' interests," the bank said in a statement.
marketscreener

Published

eulerpool
Real estate fund pulls the emergency brake: First redemption ...

businessinsider
Apollo Is Latest Private Credit Firm to Limit Redemptions
greenstreetnews.com
A Widening Pattern of Fund Gating

The move is the latest in a series of fund gates across both European real estate and U.S. private credit markets. In Germany, the €290 million Wertgrund WohnSelect D fund suspended redemptions in January — the first such halt for a German open-ended real estate mutual fund since the 2008–2012 crisis. The €1 billion Fokus Wohnen Deutschland fund followed in February, while Greenman Open, a €1.26 billion German retail property fund backed largely by Irish investors, activated its own gate in December 2025.
bloomberg
+2

In the United States, several major private credit funds have capped investor withdrawals this quarter. Apollo Global Management, Ares Management, and BlackRock's HPS Corporate Lending Fund all enforced 5% redemption caps after requests far exceeded those thresholds. Blue Owl Capital went further, halting quarterly redemptions entirely for its OBDC II fund.
businessinsider
+1

5 sources
Structural Strains in European Real Estate

The gating of UBS's Euroinvest fund reflects deeper structural challenges facing open-ended real estate funds in Germany, where investors are promised relatively easy access to capital tied up in illiquid property assets. German law permits redemption suspensions of up to three years, a provision that was introduced after the last wave of fund crises during the global financial turmoil.
eulerpool
+1

Property transaction markets in Germany have been slow to recover, with banks lending more restrictively and sales timelines stretching well beyond six months. An ING analysis forecast European real estate transaction volumes would grow roughly 14% in 2026, but activity remains well below the 2016–2022 average, with Germany among the markets posting small volume declines in 2025. The Financial Times first reported the UBS fund gating on Wednesday.
ft

European stocks drop as Trump vows more strikes on Iran

European markets opened sharply lower on Thursday as investors reacted to President Donald Trump's prime-time address the night before, in which he pledged to escalate military operations against Iran over the coming weeks, dashing hopes that the five-week-old conflict was nearing a swift resolution.

Published
2 hours ago
investing
Europe stocks open lower as Trump vows fresh Iran strikes; oil surges
barrons
Dow Set to Open Down After Trump's Iran Speech Rattles Markets
cnbc
European stocks fall as tech sector faces worst day since February 3
+54 sources
cnbc.com
Markets Reverse Rally

The pan-European Stoxx 600 fell 1.2% in early trading, while Germany's DAX dropped 1.5%, France's CAC 40 slid 1.2%, and the U.K.'s FTSE 100 declined 0.7%, according to Investing.com. The losses reversed a two-day rally that had added more than 2.5% to the regional benchmark on expectations the war was winding down. Mining and technology stocks were hit hardest, with their respective sector indexes falling 2.8% and 3%, CNBC reported.
cnbc
+1

Brent crude surged more than 6% to above $107 a barrel in early European trade, while U.S. West Texas Intermediate also jumped sharply. The spike unwound the previous session's decline and revived fears of a prolonged supply disruption through the Strait of Hormuz, which Iran has effectively blocked since hostilities began on February 28.
investing
+2

4 sources
Trump's Address Offers No Exit Timeline

Speaking from the White House on Wednesday evening, Trump said the United States would "hit them extremely hard over the next two to three weeks" and threatened to "bring them back to the Stone Ages". He reiterated a warning that the U.S. would target Iran's electricity infrastructure if Tehran did not accept a deal. While he claimed the war was "nearing completion," he offered no firm timeline for ending the conflict, according to The New York Times.
nytimes
+1

"Market sentiment has worsened overnight," Peter Sidorov, an economist at Deutsche Bank, told Barron's. He said Trump's address "offered little to no new information regarding possible timelines or conditions for ceasing hostilities against Iran".
barrons

3 sources
Broader Fallout

The selloff extended across global markets. U.S. stock futures pointed to a lower open, with S&P 500 futures down 1.3% and Nasdaq 100 futures off 1.6%. In Asia, Japan's Nikkei 225 fell 2.4%, according to Reuters. European stocks had already endured their worst month since 2022 in March, with the Stoxx 600 losing nearly 8% as oil prices surged more than 60% during the month. Eurozone inflation rose to 2.5% in March from 1.9% in February, driven by soaring energy costs, according to preliminary Eurostat data.
cnbc

Magnitude 7.4 earthquake kills one in Indonesia, triggers brief tsunami warning

A powerful undersea earthquake struck Indonesia's Molucca Sea early Thursday, toppling buildings across parts of northern Indonesia, killing at least one person, and generating small tsunami waves before warnings were lifted hours later.

Published
halifax.citynews

bbc
Tsunami warning lifted after 7.4-magnitude earthquake hits Indonesia
+12 sources
cbc.ca
Quake Rattles Eastern Indonesia

The magnitude 7.4 earthquake hit at 6:48 a.m. local time on April 2, with its epicenter roughly 120 kilometers from the city of Ternate in North Maluku province, according to the U.S. Geological Survey. The USGS initially recorded the quake at magnitude 7.8 before revising it downward. The tremor struck at a depth of about 35 kilometers, shallow enough to cause strong ground shaking across a wide area.
halifax.citynews
+4

Strong tremors lasting 10 to 20 seconds were felt in Bitung in North Sulawesi province and in Ternate, according to The Associated Press. Residents fled homes, offices, and hospitals as buildings shook. "We had just woken up and suddenly the earthquake hit… we all ran out of the house," Bitung resident Marten Mandagi told the AP.
halifax.citynews

5 sources
One Dead, Buildings Damaged

Indonesia's Search and Rescue Agency confirmed that a 70-year-old woman was killed by a building collapse in North Sulawesi, while another resident was injured. At least three additional people were hospitalized in Ternate. Footage from affected areas showed flattened homes and damaged public buildings, with frightened residents gathering in the streets.
english.news
+2

Dozens of aftershocks followed the main quake, including one measuring magnitude 6.2, as emergency teams continued damage assessments in remote communities.
euronews
+1

3 sources
Tsunami Warning Lifted

The U.S. Pacific Tsunami Warning Center initially warned of possible hazardous waves within 1,000 kilometers of the epicenter, potentially affecting coastlines in Indonesia, the Philippines, and Malaysia. Tsunami waves reaching up to 75 centimeters above normal tide levels were recorded at several monitoring stations along the Molucca Sea coast before Indonesia's meteorological agency lifted the warning. The Philippine Institute of Volcanology and Seismology said there was no destructive threat to the Philippines.
bbc
+3

Indonesia, an archipelago of more than 280 million people sitting on the Pacific "Ring of Fire," is frequently struck by earthquakes and volcanic eruptions.

Magnitude 7.3 earthquake strikes off Vanuatu coast

A magnitude 7.3 earthquake struck off the coast of Vanuatu in the South Pacific on Monday evening local time, according to the U.S. Geological Survey, with no immediate reports of damage or casualties and no tsunami threat to the wider region.
aa
+1

The quake hit at 08:44 UTC — 7:44 p.m. local time — at a depth of about 116 kilometers, with its epicenter located roughly 35 kilometers northeast of Luganville, the country's second-largest city on Santo Island. The depth of the earthquake was a key factor in limiting its destructive potential.

newsweek.com
No Tsunami Threat

The Pacific Tsunami Warning Centre determined that no tsunami threat existed from the earthquake, largely due to its depth. The Guam Homeland Security office confirmed there was no tsunami threat to the Mariana Islands, while the National Weather Service in Pago Pago likewise issued a statement confirming no threat to American Samoa.
ghs.guam
+2

The China Earthquake Networks Center recorded the quake at a depth of 140 kilometers with the epicenter at 15.25 degrees south latitude and 167.30 degrees east longitude. Anadolu Agency reported no immediate damage at the time of publication.
english.news
+1

5 sources
A Seismically Active Region

Vanuatu, an archipelago of roughly 80 islands with a population of around 300,000, sits along the Pacific Ring of Fire and is frequently rattled by seismic activity. The country has experienced a series of earthquakes in recent months, including a magnitude 6.1 quake on March 20 and a magnitude 6.4 event in February.
gdacs
+1

The nation is still recovering from a devastating magnitude 7.3 earthquake in December 2024 that struck near the capital Port Vila, killing at least 14 people and causing widespread destruction, including collapsed buildings and damaged infrastructure. That earthquake, which was far shallower at 57 kilometers deep and struck close to the populated capital, prompted a state of emergency and international aid efforts from New Zealand and Australia.
apnews

Monday's quake, by contrast, occurred at a greater depth and farther from major population centers, factors that substantially reduce the risk of damage and casualties.

Iraq's oil exports halt as Hormuz closure cuts output 70%

More than a month into the war between the United States, Israel, and Iran, Iraq's oil industry — the backbone of its economy — has been brought to its knees. Oil production across the southern province of Basra has plunged by more than 70 percent, exports from the country's main terminals have been completely halted, and hundreds of foreign workers have fled the country, according to an Associated Press report from Basra published this week.
wtop

Output across Basra province has dropped from 3.1 million barrels per day to roughly 900,000, Bassem Abdul Karim, head of the state-run Basra Oil Company, told the AP. "Exports are currently completely halted. At the moment, we are considering alternative loading areas, but none are fully operational," he said.
wtop

Published
3 hours ago
wtop
Iraq's oil hub slows to a crawl as Strait of Hormuz shutdown ... - WTOP
wikipedia
2026 Strait of Hormuz crisis - Wikipedia
aa
Iraq oil output drops nearly 60% amid US-Iran war - Anadolu Ajansı
reuters
Exclusive: Iraq oil output further plunges as storage fills ... - Reuters
cnbc.com
A Chokepoint at the Heart of the Crisis

Iraq relies on oil revenues for roughly 90 percent of its budget, and the vast majority of its crude is exported through the Strait of Hormuz, the narrow waterway at the mouth of the Persian Gulf. Iran effectively closed the strait to most commercial shipping shortly after the United States and Israel launched coordinated airstrikes on Iranian military and nuclear sites on February 28, killing Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei and more than 1,200 people, according to Iranian authorities.
wikipedia
+2

Though Iran has offered assurances that Iraqi crude could safely transit the strait, Iraq lacks its own tanker fleet and depends on chartered vessels whose owners are unwilling to accept the risk. Reuters reported in late March that production at Iraq's main southern oilfields had fallen as much as 80 percent to around 800,000 barrels per day as onshore storage filled up. Drone and missile attacks by Iran-aligned Iraqi militias have compounded the disruption, striking oil fields and energy infrastructure including facilities operated by BP and KBR.
wtop
+1

4 sources
Scrambling for Alternatives

Iraq has moved to partially offset the losses by resuming exports from its northern Kirkuk fields through a pipeline to Turkey's Mediterranean port of Ceyhan at a rate of roughly 250,000 barrels per day, following an agreement between Baghdad and the Kurdistan Regional Government. But analysts and officials say the alternative route can only provide a fraction of the lost southern capacity.
enerdata
youtube
wtop

The Iraqi government has enough reserves to cover expenses through mid-May without new oil revenue, according to economist Ahmed Tabaqchali, but after that "the government would resort to issuing bonds — but not without consequences".
wtop

3 sources
Diplomatic Push to Reopen the Strait

On Wednesday, President Trump suggested during a national address that the Strait of Hormuz would reopen "naturally" once the conflict ends, while also conditioning any ceasefire on the waterway being "open, free, and clear". The United Kingdom announced it would host a virtual conference of 35 nations on Thursday to explore strategies for reopening the strait once hostilities cease, with Prime Minister Keir Starmer warning the effort "will not be easy".
finance.yahoo
+2

Qatar's government previously dismissed pipeline-to-Europe plans as "media speculation" in early 2025, and analysts caution that major infrastructure projects would take years to complete. But the scale of the current disruption — with some 2,000 vessels stranded near the strait according to the International Maritime Organization — has given new urgency to what were once theoretical proposals.

Iraq, Turkey fast-track pipeline plans as Hormuz blockade enters fifth week

The prolonged closure of the Strait of Hormuz, now in its fifth week following the outbreak of the U.S.-Israel conflict with Iran on February 28, has forced Iraq, Turkey, and Qatar into an accelerating search for alternative energy export corridors through the Levant and Anatolia. With roughly 20% of the world's daily oil supply and a comparable share of liquefied natural gas trade severed from global markets, the crisis is reviving long-dormant pipeline projects and pushing Turkey toward a central role in Europe's energy security.
aljazeera
+1

Published
Apr 1, 2026
rudaw
Iraq plans new oil pipeline to Syria's Baniyas port: Oil ministry - Rudaw
reuters
Iraqi oil production collapses with Strait of Hormuz blocked ... - Reuters
bloomberg
Iraq Oil Output Cut Further as Baghdad Pushes for Kirkuk Restart
arabnews
Iraq plans new pipeline to Syria as oil exports slump amid regional ...
thenationalnews.com
Iraq Turns North as Southern Exports Collapse

Iraq's oil production has plummeted by roughly 70%, falling from around 4.3 million barrels per day before the conflict to approximately 1.3 million bpd, according to Reuters, as storage at southern ports reached capacity and tanker traffic through the strait ground to a halt. Iraq's Oil Ministry announced in late March that it is studying the construction of an entirely new pipeline to the Syrian Mediterranean port of Baniyas, part of a broader Basra-Haditha corridor that would include branches toward Jordan and Syria. Deputy Oil Minister Basim Mohammed Khudair told Iraq's state news agency that the old Kirkuk-Baniyas line is no longer operable due to decades of neglect and sabotage, making a rebuilt route the more viable option.
rudaw
+5

Simultaneously, Iraqi crude has begun flowing through the rehabilitated Kirkuk-Ceyhan pipeline to Turkey. Oil Minister Hayan Abdul Ghani said the line, with a capacity of 200,000 to 250,000 barrels per day, underwent final hydrostatic testing in mid-March and could bypass Kurdistan Regional Government territory entirely. Iraq aims to eventually push flows through Turkey's Ceyhan terminal to 650,000 barrels per day.
arabnews
+2

8 sources
Turkey Pitches Itself as Europe's Energy Bridge

Turkish Energy Minister Alparslan Bayraktar has seized on the crisis to argue for a far more ambitious vision. Speaking at Anadolu Agency's Editor's Desk on March 24, Bayraktar proposed extending the Kirkuk pipeline all the way south to Basra, which he said could enable up to 1.5 million barrels per day to bypass Hormuz entirely. He also raised the prospect of a pipeline carrying Qatari gas through Turkey to European markets, noting that the Hormuz blockade had exposed the fragility of seaborne LNG exports.
middleeasteye
+1

The groundwork for such a corridor has advanced. In August 2025, Turkey, Azerbaijan, Qatar, and Syria inaugurated the Turkey-Syria Natural Gas Pipeline, connecting Kilis in southern Turkey to Aleppo with a capacity of up to 6 million cubic meters per day. Bayraktar pointed to Syria's normalization as making previously unthinkable cross-border energy projects now feasible, including linking Syrian oil fields to the Iraq-Turkey pipeline.

Qatar's government previously dismissed pipeline-to-Europe plans as "media speculation" in early 2025, and analysts caution that major infrastructure projects would take years to complete. But the scale of the current disruption — with some 2,000 vessels stranded near the strait according to the International Maritime Organization — has given new urgency to what were once theoretical proposals.

Karachi Port matches full year's cargo in 24 days amid Hormuz crisis

The effective closure of the Strait of Hormuz since early March has triggered the largest energy disruption in decades, choking off roughly 20 million barrels per day of oil flow — about 20% of global petroleum consumption — and sending shockwaves through commodity markets far beyond crude.

Published
Mar 28, 2026
techi
Pakistan Emerges as Global Trade Hub as Hormuz Crisis Reroutes ...
thehilltoponline
Strait of Hormuz Closure Creates Largest Energy Disruption in ...
cnbc
Strait of Hormuz crisis explained: What it means for global shipping
thesoufancenter
One Battle After Another: No Easy Way for the U.S. to Open the Strait ...
lloydslist.com
A Chokepoint Goes Dark

Since the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps declared the waterway closed on March 2, following the launch of the U.S.-Israeli military campaign dubbed Operation Epic Fury on February 28, tanker traffic through the 21-mile-wide passage has plunged by more than 90%, according to ship-tracking data. Iran has conducted at least 21 confirmed attacks on merchant vessels, and major shipping lines including Maersk and MSC have suspended all transits. Protection and indemnity insurers canceled coverage for the zone beginning March 5, rendering the strait commercially unnavigable.
cnbc
+2

More than 500 vessels remain stranded in the Persian Gulf, and Gulf oil exports have fallen by roughly 60%. President Trump has threatened to destroy Iran's civilian power plants unless Tehran allows full freedom of navigation, while Iran has selectively permitted some vessels — notably Indian and Chinese ships — to pass, and has imposed a reported $2 million toll on transiting vessels. A UN Security Council resolution adopted March 11 called on Iran to halt provocations, but no country has committed forces to a joint escort operation.
thehilltoponline
+1
youtube
rbc

6 sources
Beyond Oil: Fertilizer, Helium, and Food

The blockade's reach extends well past energy markets. QatarEnergy, which supplies about 20% of the world's LNG, declared force majeure after drone attacks damaged its Ras Laffan export terminal. The Economist reported that the Gulf region accounts for 45% of global sulfur exports, 22% of the urea trade, and a third of commercial helium production — all now bottlenecked. Fortune reported that about 15% of goods transiting Hormuz are non-energy materials critical to agriculture and manufacturing.
thenationalnews
+3

Fertilizer prices have surged, with urea reaching approximately $591 per tonne, up 25% since the war began, according to The National. Analysts at Fitch Ratings warned that 30% to 35% of global nitrogen fertilizers flow through the strait, and Indian fertilizer plants have already cut output as supplies dry up. Helium shortages could persist for months even after fighting stops, because Qatar's gas facilities sustained damage and specialized cryogenic transport containers must be repositioned, according to Politico.
politico
+1

5 sources
Karachi Emerges as Unlikely Winner

Pakistan's Karachi Port has become an unexpected beneficiary of the rerouting. In just the first 24 days of March, the port processed 8,313 transshipment containers — matching its entire 2025 annual volume, a 1,423% surge. South Asia Pakistan Terminal handled the largest share, while a new feeder service launched March 11 now connects Karachi to the UAE ports of Fujairah and Khor Fakkan outside the exclusion zone. Whether Karachi can sustain this pace remains uncertain; the port is approaching operational capacity, and congestion could eventually push carriers toward alternatives like Salalah or India's Mundra.

The Iran war's economic shockwaves are now rippling through American living rooms and Latin American bond markets alike. Mortgage Rates Climb as Oil Keeps the Fed on Hold

Mortgage rates in the United States have risen sharply since the conflict between the U.S., Israel, and Iran erupted on February 28, with the 30-year fixed refinance rate reaching nearly 7% by late March, according to data from Zillow cited by multiple outlets. The 30-year fixed purchase rate hit 6.47% as of March 28, its highest since late September, while Bankrate reported the average 30-year fixed-refinance rate climbed 7 basis points in a single week to 6.69% as of March 26.

Chile's Inflation Shock Reshapes Bond Market

Half a world away, Chile is confronting the oil crisis head-on. The government loosened its fuel price stabilization mechanism last week, triggering a roughly 30% jump in gasoline prices and as much as 54% for diesel — the steepest increase since at least 1980. The move, announced by Finance Minister Jorge Quiroz, came after the administration determined it could no longer afford to shield consumers from the international oil shock.
usnews
+1

The result has been swift. Chile's one-year breakeven inflation rate — a gauge of market expectations — leaped almost 20 basis points in a single day to 4.95%, its highest since March 2023, and has risen 238 basis points in March alone, according to Bloomberg. The central bank raised its year-end 2026 inflation forecast to 4% from 3.2% and held its key rate at 4.5%, shelving a cut that analysts had widely expected before the war.
bloomberg
+2

The shift underscores how quickly the war has reversed Chile's inflation progress; annual consumer price growth had fallen to just 2.4% in February, a nearly six-year low.

The economic fallout from the US-Iran war is rippling across Europe with mounting force, as fresh data on Friday showed inflation accelerating in Spain, governments in Germany and Italy moved to slash growth forecasts, and the European Central Bank warned the conflict could destabilize financial markets.

reuters.com
Inflation Surges in Spain as Energy Costs Bite

Spain became the first major European economy to report March inflation figures, and the numbers were stark. Consumer prices rose 3.3% year-on-year, up from 2.5% in February, according to flash data from the Spanish National Statistics Institute (INE) — the highest rate since June 2024. The main driver was a sharp rise in the price of fuels and lubricants linked to Iran's blockade of the Strait of Hormuz. The jump came despite a €5 billion emergency package approved by Madrid on March 20, which included VAT reductions on energy bills and fuel subsidies. Angel Talavera, Oxford Economics' chief economist for Europe, told El Pais: "It's a sharp increase, but it could have been worse. We need to wait and see the breakdown of fuels and electricity to understand the exact impact of the government's measures".
euronews
+2

3 sources
Germany and Italy Brace for Slower Growth

The conflict is forcing governments across the euro area to reconsider their economic outlook. According to Bloomberg, German officials see a risk that growth could halve to just 0.5% this year if the war drags on, down from a prior projection of 1%. The IMK institute said on Thursday that even its base case now calls for 0.9% growth, down from an earlier estimate of 1.2%. Italy's government is set to cut its own 2026 forecast to as low as 0.5%, from a current 0.7%, according to Bloomberg, with the revised figure expected in April. Italy's leading business lobby, Confindustria, warned that GDP could stagnate entirely if hostilities extend into the second quarter.
money.usnews
+3

The Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development on Thursday left its global growth forecast unchanged at 2.9% but sharply raised inflation projections, forecasting G20 inflation at 4% — up from 2.8% predicted in December. Euro area GDP growth is now expected to slip to 0.8% in 2026.

ECB Vice President Luis de Guindos said on Thursday that while euro area banks have limited direct exposure to the Middle East, the war "could trigger the unravelling of interconnected vulnerabilities and cause systemic stress". He cautioned that high asset valuations could lead to a sharp repricing of risk for leveraged borrowers and sovereigns. European shares fell on Friday, with the STOXX Europe 600 trading lower as investors weighed the twin threats of higher inflation and weaker growth.

Spain's Regional Governments Mobilize Over €2.3 Billion in Response to Iran Crisis

Spanish regional governments have deployed their own aid packages totaling over €2.3 billion to address the economic consequences of the Middle East conflict, according to a report compiled by Europa Press. The measures, focused on supporting businesses, self-employed workers, and productive sectors exposed to rising energy costs, complement the national government's €5 billion plan approved through Royal Decree-Law 7/2026 on March 20.

Basque Country and Catalonia Lead Regional Response

The Basque Country has been the region with the highest spending, with an industrial shield of 1.047 billion euros structured around four pillars: employment protection (105 million), financial support for SMEs (450 million in loans), business transformation and diversification (277 million, 51.4% more than in 2025), and energy autonomy (215 million), as announced by the Basque Government.
euskadi

Catalonia approved an initial package of 400 million that includes direct aid, tax exemptions, and financing for families to cover food and energy expenses, as announced by president Salvador Illa. The Valencia Region has mobilized more than 300 million, with a subsidized credit line of 100 million through the Institut Valencià de Finances and tax reductions, as reported by El Independiente.

Other Regional Governments Round Out the Aid Package Map

Castilla y León approved 28 measures totaling 169 million euros from its own funds, which reach an impact of 286.7 million when combined with state tax cuts. The bulk of it, 113 million, is allocated to business financing, with loans of up to 750,000 euros. The Balearic Islands will mobilize more than 160 million, including 36.7 million in direct aid to sectors such as agriculture and transport, plus 75 million in credit lines. The Canary Islands, whose tax system excludes the direct application of state VAT cuts, reached an agreement with the central government for a package of 29.8 million for 100 days, expandable to 60 million annually if the conflict continues.

An Unprecedented State Shield as a Backdrop

The central government's plan, validated by Congress on March 25 with only Vox voting against it, includes reducing VAT on electricity and fuel from 21% to 10%, lowering the Special Electricity Tax to 0.5%, and a 20-cent-per-liter rebate on professional diesel for transporters, farmers, and fishermen. President Pedro Sánchez stated that with these measures "Spain will become the country with the largest social and economic shield in the entire EU" in response to the conflict. Regions such as Andalusia, Castilla-La Mancha, Extremadura, and Aragon have not yet announced specific packages linked to the war's impact.

IMF says France, Spain better shielded from energy crisis

The International Monetary Fund warned on Monday that the war in the Middle East is "dimming the outlook for many economies," but singled out France and Spain as relatively better positioned within Europe to absorb the energy shock roiling global markets since the conflict began in early March.
imf

In a blog post authored by senior officials across six IMF departments, the Fund said Italy and the United Kingdom are "especially exposed by their reliance on gas-fired power," while France and Spain are "relatively protected by their greater nuclear and renewables capacity". The assessment marks the IMF's most detailed public commentary yet on how the crisis is splitting Europe along energy-mix lines.
imf

Is Europe going to be forced to return to nuclear energy?
yahoo.com
The Strait of Hormuz and Europe's Gas Vulnerability

The de facto closure of the Strait of Hormuz — through which roughly 25 to 30 percent of global oil and 20 percent of liquefied natural gas flow — has produced what the International Energy Agency has called "the largest supply disruption in the history of the global oil market". European benchmark gas futures on the Dutch Title Transfer Facility have surged roughly 60 percent since the start of the conflict, according to Le Monde, rising from around €30 to over €50 per megawatt hour.
wikipedia
+2

France generates about 65 percent of its electricity from nuclear power and exports surpluses to neighbors, according to Euronews, giving it insulation from gas-price volatility. Spain, meanwhile, has invested heavily in wind and solar capacity. By contrast, Italy and the UK remain dependent on gas-fired generation, leaving them acutely sensitive to the supply squeeze now gripping LNG markets.
euronews

4 sources
Broader Economic Fallout

The IMF stopped short of issuing revised growth forecasts, saying a fuller assessment would come with its World Economic Outlook on April 14. But the blog outlined how the energy shock is acting as "a large, sudden tax on income" for fuel-importing economies worldwide.
imf

BNP Paribas economists forecast eurozone inflation accelerating to 2.6 percent year-on-year in March, with Spain reaching 3.3 percent and Germany 2.8 percent, driven largely by rising energy costs. In France, electricity prices are less directly tied to gas because of the country's nuclear fleet, though broader inflationary pressures remain.

Latin America scrambles to contain fuel costs as Iran war drives oil surge

The U.S.-Israeli military campaign against Iran, now entering its second month, is forcing Latin American governments into emergency measures as oil prices that have surged more than 40% since late February ripple through their economies. From Mexico City to Montevideo, policymakers are deploying subsidies, price caps, and biofuel mandates to shield consumers from a crisis that analysts warn could worsen if the Strait of Hormuz remains effectively closed.

Mexico extends its gas price cap as the Iran war spikes oil prices
en.mercopress.com
Price Caps and Subsidies From Mexico to Uruguay

Mexico has emerged as the region's most aggressive intervener. President Claudia Sheinbaum renewed a voluntary agreement with gas station operators covering 96% of the country's service stations to keep regular gasoline below 24 pesos per liter for another six months. The government has simultaneously ramped up tax credits on the IEPS excise tax for diesel imports, with the Ministry of Finance absorbing rising crude costs through fiscal incentives that have pushed the tax's share of pump prices to their lowest levels in years. Analysts note that while the strategy keeps retail prices stable, it carries a growing fiscal cost as international benchmarks remain elevated.
globaltradealert
+3

Uruguay took a different path on Friday, announcing a 7% fuel price increase effective April 1 and shifting from bimonthly to monthly price adjustments to better track volatile markets. Economy Minister Gabriel Oddone said the government capped the increase well below what market conditions would dictate — without intervention, gasoline would have risen 13% and diesel 44%. "We have not had oil market disruption events since the 1970s," Oddone said, comparing the crisis to Iraq's invasion of Kuwait.
mercopress

5 sources
Argentina, Colombia, and Ecuador Navigate the Shock

Argentina on Friday moved to allow firms to voluntarily blend up to 15% ethanol into gasoline, up from the current 12% mandate, seeking to reduce dependence on costlier petroleum-based fuels, according to Reuters. The measure builds on existing biofuel legislation and leverages the country's substantial corn and sugarcane ethanol production capacity.
reuters
+1

Colombia occupies a paradoxical position: as Latin America's fifth-largest oil producer, it benefits from prices that have blown past the $59.20 per barrel assumed in its 2026 budget. But the country's fuel price stabilization fund continues to accumulate debt — the diesel subsidy now exceeds 3,500 pesos per gallon — while Moody's projects the fiscal deficit will exceed 6% of GDP for a third consecutive year. A senior central bank board member called the war a "major threat" to an economy already grappling with unanchored inflation expectations.
bloomberg
+2

Ecuador faces perhaps the steepest structural challenge. The country's three refineries process roughly 175,000 barrels per day against domestic demand of 291,000 barrels, leaving it heavily reliant on imported refined products. Gasoline prices hit near-record levels in mid-March, and petroleum expert Nelson Baldeón warned that sustained crude prices between $100 and $110 per barrel could dramatically expand the fiscal deficit. The country spent $6.2 billion importing fuel in 2025 alone.
transoceanica

For Latin America, where economists estimate every $10 increase in oil prices can add up to 0.4 percentage points to regional inflation, the stakes extend well beyond the pump.

Spain's inflation jumps to 3.3% as Iran war rattles Europe's economy

The economic fallout from the US-Iran war is rippling across Europe with mounting force, as fresh data on Friday showed inflation accelerating in Spain, governments in Germany and Italy moved to slash growth forecasts, and the European Central Bank warned the conflict could destabilize financial markets.

Published

wsj
Spanish Inflation Jumps on Iran War - WSJ
money.usnews
Iran Conflict Threatens to Stall Germany's Economic Growth, IMK Says
reuters.com
Inflation Surges in Spain as Energy Costs Bite

Spain became the first major European economy to report March inflation figures, and the numbers were stark. Consumer prices rose 3.3% year-on-year, up from 2.5% in February, according to flash data from the Spanish National Statistics Institute (INE) — the highest rate since June 2024. The main driver was a sharp rise in the price of fuels and lubricants linked to Iran's blockade of the Strait of Hormuz. The jump came despite a €5 billion emergency package approved by Madrid on March 20, which included VAT reductions on energy bills and fuel subsidies. Angel Talavera, Oxford Economics' chief economist for Europe, told El Pais: "It's a sharp increase, but it could have been worse. We need to wait and see the breakdown of fuels and electricity to understand the exact impact of the government's measures".
euronews
+2

3 sources
Germany and Italy Brace for Slower Growth

The conflict is forcing governments across the euro area to reconsider their economic outlook. According to Bloomberg, German officials see a risk that growth could halve to just 0.5% this year if the war drags on, down from a prior projection of 1%. The IMK institute said on Thursday that even its base case now calls for 0.9% growth, down from an earlier estimate of 1.2%. Italy's government is set to cut its own 2026 forecast to as low as 0.5%, from a current 0.7%, according to Bloomberg, with the revised figure expected in April. Italy's leading business lobby, Confindustria, warned that GDP could stagnate entirely if hostilities extend into the second quarter.
money.usnews
+3

The Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development on Thursday left its global growth forecast unchanged at 2.9% but sharply raised inflation projections, forecasting G20 inflation at 4% — up from 2.8% predicted in December. Euro area GDP growth is now expected to slip to 0.8% in 2026.
reuters
+2

7 sources
ECB Warns of Systemic Risk

ECB Vice President Luis de Guindos said on Thursday that while euro area banks have limited direct exposure to the Middle East, the war "could trigger the unravelling of interconnected vulnerabilities and cause systemic stress". He cautioned that high asset valuations could lead to a sharp repricing of risk for leveraged borrowers and sovereigns. European shares fell on Friday, with the STOXX Europe 600 trading lower as investors weighed the twin threats of higher inflation and weaker growth.

Trump Tells Oil-Dependent Countries to Protect Hormuz or Buy U.S. Crude

U.S. President Donald Trump on Wednesday urged nations dependent on oil transiting through the Strait of Hormuz to buy American crude or take responsibility themselves for reopening the waterway, in a televised address from the White House that marks a shift in Washington's stance on the global energy crisis triggered by the war with Iran.

A War Shaking Global Markets

The conflict between the United States, Israel, and Iran erupted on February 28, 2026, following joint attacks against Iranian territory. Trump tells allies to reopen Strait of Hormuz themselves

President Donald Trump on Tuesday urged nations dependent on oil shipments through the Strait of Hormuz to either purchase fuel from the United States or take military action to reopen the waterway themselves, marking a sharp pivot away from earlier promises to secure the critical passage.

"All of those countries that can't get jet fuel because of the Strait of Hormuz, like the United Kingdom, which refused to get involved in the decapitation of Iran, I have a suggestion for you: Number 1, buy from the U.S., we have plenty, and Number 2, build up some delayed courage, go to the Strait, and just TAKE IT," Trump wrote on Truth Social. Iran's Parliament Approves Hormuz Strait Toll Plan
reuters.com
Iran Formalizes Control

Iran's parliamentary National Security and Foreign Policy Committee on Monday approved the Strait of Hormuz Management Plan, which includes eight key measures: a rial-based toll system for transiting vessels, a ban on passage for American and Israeli ships, restrictions on countries participating in sanctions against Iran, and cooperation with Oman to establish a legal framework. According to Lloyd's List Intelligence, Iran's Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps had already established a de facto "toll booth" regime, with at least two ships reported to have paid fees in Chinese yuan. The legislation aims to formalize what has been an informal system since Iran sealed the strait following U.S.-Israeli strikes that began on February 28.

NASA's Artemis II crew orbits Earth after historic moonshot launch

NASA's four Artemis II astronauts have reached a stable orbit, clearing the first critical milestone of their journey to the Moon. The crew's Orion capsule successfully separated from the Space Launch System rocket and completed its initial orbital checks, with a trans-lunar injection burn planned for Thursday evening that will send them on their way to the lunar surface.

Published
10 hours ago
nasa
Artemis II Flight Update: Apogee Raise Burn Complete, Crew Looks Ahead to Proximity Operations
cbsnews
Artemis II crew begins "crazy first day" in space after exhilarating launch
foxnews
Artemis launch live: NASA Artemis II launch time, countdown and updates
+22 sources
nasa.gov
A "Crazy First Day" in Orbit

The Space Launch System rocket launched at 6:35 p.m. EDT on April 1, 2026, from Launch Complex 39B, producing nearly 9 million pounds of thrust as it carried Commander Reid Wiseman, Pilot Victor Glover, Mission Specialists Christina Koch and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen into space. The mission marks the first time a woman, a Black astronaut and a Canadian will travel to the Moon.
foxnews
+2

The crew spent their first 24 hours in a highly elliptical Earth orbit, putting Orion through exhaustive system checks. "It is a crazy first day," Wiseman told CBS News, describing the need to verify that the capsule can scrub carbon dioxide, provide drinking water and handle basic human functions before pressing on toward the Moon.
cbsnews

Not everything went smoothly. Koch reported a fault light while checking out the capsule's toilet system shortly after reaching orbit. Flight controllers told the crew the toilet could not spin up and advised using contingency bags for urine collection while engineers worked on a repair plan.
nasa
+1

4 sources
Proximity Operations and Next Steps

NASA confirmed that the apogee raise burn was successfully completed, fine-tuning Orion's orbit. A key early milestone came when Glover took manual control of the spacecraft and maneuvered it relative to the detached upper stage of the SLS rocket during a roughly 70-minute proximity operations demonstration. Glover described the thruster firing as producing "a little rumble, like driving on a rocky road".
cbsnews
+1

The crew was expected to take two four-hour rest periods early Thursday before NASA's mission management team reviews Orion's performance and clears the spacecraft for the trans-lunar injection burn. That six-minute engine firing, planned for Thursday evening, will increase the capsule's velocity by about 900 mph and send it on a free-return trajectory around the Moon.
cbsnews

2 sources
The Road to the Moon and Beyond

The approximately 10-day mission will carry the crew on a loop around the Moon without landing or entering lunar orbit. The astronauts are expected to pass within about 4,100 miles of the lunar surface and surpass the distance record set by Apollo 13 in 1970. Splashdown is targeted for April 10 in the Pacific Ocean off Southern California.
foxnews
+2

"This is a test flight," NASA Administrator Jared Isaacman told CBS News. "This is the opening act in a series of missions that will send astronauts to and from the moon with great frequency as we return to stay".
cbsnews

Artemis II toilet reports fault light hours after historic moon mission launch

Hours after the Artemis II crew made history Wednesday by launching on humanity's first lunar voyage in more than 53 years, mission specialist Christina Koch reported a glitch with the Orion capsule's toilet — the Universal Waste Management System — during early systems checks in orbit. "The toilet shut down on its own, and I have a blinking amber fault light," Koch told Mission Control, according to the Associated Press. She was advised to use a handheld bag as a backup while ground teams investigated the issue.
seattletimes
+2

The fault light arrived during what was otherwise a smooth start to the approximately 10-day mission. The four-person crew — commander Reid Wiseman, pilot Victor Glover, Koch, and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen — lifted off at 6:35 p.m. EDT from Kennedy Space Center's Launch Complex 39B. The astronauts reached orbit and began a planned 25-hour checkout phase circling Earth before firing Orion's main engine to head for the moon.
space

Artemis II Astronauts Are Getting a Major Space Toilet Upgrade ...
cbc

mensjournal.com
A Giant Leap for Bathroom Technology

The toilet is one of the most talked-about upgrades aboard Orion. During the Apollo missions of the late 1960s and early 1970s, astronauts urinated into roll-on cuffs and defecated into plastic bags in full view of their crewmates. The new system, adapted from the International Space Station's waste management hardware, sits inside a small private stall — complete with a door and privacy curtains — roughly the size of a lavatory on a small passenger jet.
vice
+2

The titanium toilet uses air suction rather than water and gravity to direct waste, with separate collection for liquid and solid waste. Urine is vented into space several times a day, while solid waste is stored in canisters and returned to Earth. Each astronaut has an individual funnel for the urine hose to maintain hygiene.
space
+2

4 sources
"The One Place We Can Feel Alone"

Hansen, making his spaceflight debut, highlighted the toilet's role in crew well-being during a Canadian Space Agency vlog last October. "We're pretty fortunate as a crew to have a toilet with a door on this tiny spacecraft," he said. It is "the one place that we can go during the mission where we can actually feel like we're alone for a moment".
aol
+1

NASA anticipated the possibility of a malfunction. Debbie Korth, deputy Orion Program manager, said before launch that the crew is carrying contingency equipment including urine collection bags. "They can still use the toilet for other functions, even without it functioning, to be able to dump the urine overboard," Korth said.

NASA's Artemis II set to launch Wednesday with unprecedented medical research

As NASA prepares to launch Artemis II on Wednesday, April 1, the mission represents more than a return to lunar orbit — it is poised to become the most medically instrumented deep-space flight in history. For the first time since Apollo 17 in 1972, astronauts will travel beyond Earth's protective magnetic field, and scientists plan to study the biological toll of that journey at a cellular level that was unimaginable during the Apollo era.
science.nasa
+1

Mar 31, 2026

To Protect Artemis II Astronauts, NASA Experts Keep Eyes on Sun
gizmodo
NASA's Artemis 2 Will Test Human Health in Deep Space Like ...
skyatnightmagazine
Artemis II astronauts are taking their own avatars to the Moon, to find ...
science
As humans return to the Moon, scientists confront the dangers of ...
mashable.com
Radiation Beyond Earth's Shield

The 10-day mission will carry NASA astronauts Reid Wiseman, Victor Glover, and Christina Koch, along with Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen, through the Van Allen radiation belts and into the galactic cosmic radiation environment beyond Earth's magnetosphere. According to NASA, the expected radiation dose for the trip is comparable to a one-month stay on the International Space Station, or roughly 5% of an astronaut's career exposure limit. The journal Science has likened it to the dose from a whole-body CT scan.
gizmodo
+2

The greater concern is unpredictable solar particle events. NASA's Moon to Mars Space Weather Analysis Office and NOAA's Space Weather Prediction Center will monitor the Sun around the clock during the flight. If radiation levels inside the Orion capsule spike, an alarm system will alert the crew. At higher thresholds, astronauts are trained to reconfigure their cabin, pulling stored equipment from storage bays and positioning it as shielding between themselves and incoming particles — a radiation shelter procedure the crew plans to rehearse on the mission's eighth day.
science.nasa
+1

4 sources
Organ Chips and Personal Dosimeters

Among the most novel experiments aboard is AVATAR (A Virtual Astronaut Tissue Analog Response), which will send organ-on-a-chip devices containing each astronaut's own bone marrow cells into deep space for the first time. The USB-sized chips, built by biotechnology firm Emulate Inc. and housed in a compact laboratory from Space Tango, mimic the function of living tissue. After recovery, researchers will use single-cell RNA sequencing to compare the spaceflight chips against ground-control samples, measuring how radiation and microgravity altered gene expression at the individual cell level.
facebook
+3

Each crew member will also carry a Crew Active Dosimeter developed by Mirion Technologies in collaboration with NASA's Johnson Space Center, providing real-time, personal radiation exposure data throughout the flight. Inside the capsule, six sensors from the Hybrid Electronic Radiation Assessor system will track dose rates in different cabin zones.
mirion
+1

6 sources
A New Era for Aerospace Medicine

The mission's health research agenda extends beyond radiation. NASA's Human Research Program will collect data on fluid shifts, vestibular disruption, immune system changes, and crew behavioral health using wearable ARCHER sensors and saliva swabs measuring stress hormones. UCF's recently established Center for Aerospace and Extreme Environments Medicine is among the institutions working to translate deep-space health findings into clinical innovations on Earth, from cancer treatment insights to personalized medicine.
youtube
ucf
+1

"Each tissue chip is a tiny sample uniquely created so that we can examine how the effects of deep space act on each human explorer," said Nicky Fox, NASA's associate administrator for the Science Mission Directorate.
skyatnightmagazine

X-class solar flare hits Earth days before Artemis 2 launch

With NASA targeting an April 1 liftoff for Artemis II, the first crewed mission beyond low Earth orbit since Apollo 17 in 1972, the Sun offered a timely reminder of the dangers awaiting the four-person crew. A powerful X1.4 solar flare erupted early on March 30, triggering radio blackouts across parts of southeast Asia and Australia and launching a coronal mass ejection with a possible Earth-directed component, according to NOAA's Space Weather Prediction Center. NASA said the flare is not currently anticipated to impact the mission but that the agency is continuing to monitor space weather activity.
space
+1

The flare underscores a central challenge of the 10-day lunar flyby: once astronauts Reid Wiseman, Victor Glover, Christina Koch, and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen leave the protective cocoon of Earth's magnetic field, they will be exposed to solar flares, coronal mass ejections, and galactic cosmic rays with little natural shielding.
wikipedia
+1

To Protect Artemis II Astronauts, NASA Experts Keep Eyes on Sun
space
Powerful X-class solar flare triggers radio blackout ahead of Artemis ...
swpc.noaa
SWPC Decision-Support for Artemis II
aerospaceglobalnews
NASA's Artemis II has a new problem: Solar flares
scitechdaily.com
A Round-the-Clock Watch on the Sun

NASA and NOAA have built a layered monitoring system to protect the crew in real time. NOAA's Space Weather Prediction Center will provide specialized decision-support for the entire mission, working directly with NASA's Space Radiation Analysis Group at Johnson Space Center in Houston. Meanwhile, NASA's Moon to Mars Space Weather Analysis Office at Goddard Space Flight Center will continuously assess solar eruptions and share findings with the Johnson team.
swpc.noaa
+1

"Our focus will be real-time space weather analysis, prioritizing solar energetic particles and events that could produce them," said Mary Aronne, operations lead for the Goddard office. "We're looking for the trigger, which would typically be a flare or a coronal mass ejection."
science.nasa

The teams will draw on data from spacecraft positioned across the solar system, including NASA's Perseverance rover on Mars, which can observe sunspots on the far side of the Sun up to two weeks before they rotate into Earth's view.
science.nasa

2 sources
Orion's Built-In Defenses

Inside the Orion capsule, six radiation sensors measure dose rates across the cabin, while astronauts will wear personal dosimeters. If radiation levels spike, onboard systems trigger audible alarms. At higher thresholds, the crew is trained to reconfigure their cabin, repositioning stowed equipment to add shielding mass between themselves and incoming particles — a procedure that will be tested for the first time on this mission.
science.nasa

The baseline radiation exposure from passing through the Van Allen belts and galactic cosmic rays is expected to be comparable to a one-month stay on the International Space Station, roughly 5 percent of an astronaut's career limit, according to NASA. Any solar storm exposure would add to that total.
science.nasa

1 source
A Volatile Sun Adds Urgency

The Sun is in an active phase of Solar Cycle 25, and some researchers have argued NASA should delay the flight. A team led by Dr. Victor Velasco Herrera of the National Autonomous University of Mexico warned that a high-risk window for powerful eruptions could extend through mid-2026. NASA has pressed ahead with an April 1 launch window opening at 6:24 p.m. EDT, with backup opportunities through April 6. NOAA has issued a moderate geomagnetic storm watch for March 31 following the latest flare.
aerospaceglobalnews

Ángel Simón Replaces Escribano as Chairman of Indra After His Resignation

Ángel Escribano submitted his resignation this Wednesday as director and executive chairman of Indra at an extraordinary board meeting, ending his 14 months at the helm of the defense and technology company. In a letter sent to the National Securities Market Commission (CNMV), Escribano stated that "the events of recent weeks have created a situation that, in addition to personal wear and tear, threatens to compromise the objectives that drove me from day one."

Clash with Moncloa

Escribano's departure came after weeks of friction with the government, which—through the State Society for Industrial Participations (SEPI), Indra's largest shareholder with 28% of the capital—pressured for his resignation. The conflict intensified around the failed integration of Escribano Mechanical & Engineering (EM&E), the Escribano brothers' family company, into Indra. SEPI considered that Escribano's dual role as owner of EM&E and chairman of Indra represented an irreconcilable conflict of interest.

According to El Confidencial, the government made public contracts conditional on Escribano's departure. Despite having resisted an initial removal attempt by demonstrating the board's support, according to Vozpópuli, Escribano ultimately gave in.

Intel plans $15M more for startup chaired by its CEO

Intel has planned to invest an additional $15 million in SambaNova, the AI chip startup where Intel CEO Lip-Bu Tan serves as executive chairman, according to a Reuters review of corporate records reported on Wednesday. The planned investment adds to the chipmaker's existing financial commitment to SambaNova and renews scrutiny over Tan's overlapping roles at both companies.

reuters.com
A Deepening Financial Relationship

The $15 million would come on top of Intel's participation in SambaNova's $350 million Series E funding round, announced in February, which was led by Vista Equity Partners and Cambium Capital. Reuters had previously reported that Intel planned to invest around $100 million in that round, with potential commitments of up to $150 million. Intel Capital, the company's venture arm, provided what SambaNova described as "strong participation" in the round.
reuters
+4

Tan has served as SambaNova's executive chairman since May 2024 and became Intel's CEO on March 18, 2025. His venture capital firm, Walden International, co-led SambaNova's $56 million Series A round in 2018. Reuters reported in December 2025 that Intel had pursued deals that could boost Tan's personal fortune, prompting internal policy changes that require the CEO to recuse himself from conflicted decisions, with CFO David Zinsner handling such matters instead. Intel's board had earlier blocked Tan's attempt to acquire another startup, Rivos, citing his direct financial interest in that company.

A Busy Week for Intel

The SambaNova news caps a busy stretch for Intel. On Tuesday, the company also announced a $14.2 billion agreement to repurchase the 49 percent equity stake in its Fab 34 manufacturing facility in Ireland from Apollo Global Management. Apollo had acquired the minority stake in 2024 for $11.2 billion, and Intel said it would fund the buyback through cash on hand and roughly $6.5 billion in new debt.
newsroom.intel

The two companies framed the deal as a sign of Intel's improving financial position. Intel said the repurchase "reflects continued business momentum underpinned by the growing and essential role CPUs play in the era of AI".

SambaNova's Rising Profile

SambaNova, based in San Jose, California, builds chips for AI inference workloads and positions itself as an alternative to Nvidia in the data center market. The startup unveiled its next-generation SN50 chip alongside the February funding round, claiming it delivers five times faster compute than competing chips. SoftBank has signed on as the first customer to deploy the SN50 in AI data centers in Japan. Intel and SambaNova also announced a multiyear collaboration to deliver AI inference solutions using Intel Xeon processors alongside SambaNova's accelerators.

Nepal charges 32 in $20M Everest helicopter rescue scam

Nepalese authorities have filed organized crime and fraud charges against 32 people in connection with a sprawling scheme that allegedly bilked international travel insurers out of nearly $20 million through fake helicopter rescues on Mount Everest and other Himalayan peaks.

Published
14 hours ago
occrp
Poisoned Trekkers and Phantom Flights: Nepal Charges 32 in ...
kathmandupost
Inside Nepal's fake rescue racket - The Kathmandu Post
nytimes
Nepal Arrests 6 Officials, Accusing Them of Fraudulent Everest ...
timesofindia.indiatimes
Everest guides accused of poisoning trekkers for insurance payouts
thetimes.com
Poisoned Food and Phantom Flights

The charges, filed on March 12 in Kathmandu District Court, implicate trekking agency owners, helicopter operators, and hospital executives accused of running a coordinated fraud network between 2022 and 2025. Nine suspects appeared in court, while 23 others remain at large.
occrp
+1

At the heart of the scheme, according to investigators from Nepal's Central Investigation Bureau, guides secretly laced tourists' food with baking soda — a known laxative — to induce vomiting and diarrhea that mimicked altitude sickness or food poisoning. Once trekkers were incapacitated, guides pressured them into agreeing to expensive helicopter evacuations. Operators then forged medical reports and flight records, billing each multi-passenger helicopter trip as multiple separate rescues to inflate payouts.
kathmandupost
+2

"A charge sheet has been filed at the court," said Dipak Kumar Shrestha, a spokesperson for the Kathmandu District Court. "The court is recording statements of the accused, giving high priority to this high-profile corruption case."
occrp

3 sources
A Network Worth Millions

Police records show the network fraudulently obtained at least $19.69 million in insurance payouts. Mountain Rescue Service P. Ltd. allegedly orchestrated 171 fraudulent rescues out of 1,248 total flights, claiming roughly $10.3 million. Nepal Charter Service P. Ltd. is accused of siphoning approximately $8.2 million, while Everest Experience and Assistance P. Ltd. was linked to about $1.1 million in fraudulent claims. Prosecutors are seeking 1.51 billion Nepalese rupees — about $11.3 million — in total fines.
timesofindia.indiatimes
+1

According to the Kathmandu Post, hospitals played a central role, with Era International Hospital alone receiving more than $15.87 million in deposits linked to the scheme. Hospitals allegedly paid 20 to 25 percent of insurance payouts to trekking companies and a similar share to helicopter operators in exchange for patient referrals.
kathmandupost

3 sources
A Long-Running Problem

The fraud has long been an open secret in Nepal's adventure tourism industry. Reports of baking soda poisoning and inflated rescue bills surfaced as early as 2018, when a government probe found that 35 percent of helicopter evacuations were fraudulent. That investigation led to no disciplinary action, and several major international insurers, including Travellers Assists, stopped selling coverage for Nepal treks altogether.
outsideonline
+2

The new charges land just as Nepal's spring climbing season opens, with nearly 500 climbers expected to attempt Everest this year. Authorities have introduced new rules mandating formal reporting of all rescue operations — a step aimed at restoring trust in an industry central to the country's economy.
ndtv

Safesea calls for international probe into deadly tanker attack near Iraq

Safesea Group, a New Jersey-based shipping company, has called for an independent international investigation into the March 11 attack on its crude oil tanker MT Safesea Vishnu near Iraq's Khor Al Zubair port, describing the assault as a coordinated operation that poses a direct threat to global shipping and trade stability. The call, made public this week by Safesea Group Chairman Dr. S.V. Anchan, comes as war risk insurance premiums for vessels transiting the Persian Gulf have surged to historically unprecedented levels.
spglobal
+3

Published
16 hours ago

Safesea Calls For International Probe After Deadly Tanker Attack ...
spglobal
War risk insurance cost off highs but still elevated in Persian Gulf
reuters
Maritime insurance premiums surge as Iran conflict widens - Reuters
telegraphindia
Indian national killed in Iran attack on US-owned oil tanker Safesea ...
safeseagroup.com
A "Deliberate and Calculated" Strike

The Marshall Islands-flagged Safesea Vishnu was anchored in Iraqi territorial waters, conducting routine ship-to-ship loading of roughly 53,000 metric tonnes of naphtha, when it was struck by what Iraqi port officials and maritime analysts described as an explosive-laden unmanned boat. The attack killed Deonandan Singh, a 55-year-old senior crew member from Mumbai, and forced the remaining 27 crew members to abandon ship as fires engulfed the vessel. A second tanker, the Maltese-flagged Zefyros, was also attacked in the same area that night, prompting Iraq to suspend all oil terminal operations.
telegraphindia
+2

Iran's Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps claimed it struck the Safesea Vishnu after the vessel "ignored warnings and alerts," according to a statement carried by Iranian state media. Safesea Group has rejected that framing. Anchan said the sequence of events suggests "a highly coordinated and pre-planned operation involving surveillance, precise execution and possible real-time monitoring". The company noted that unidentified high-speed boats were observed circling anchored vessels a full day before the attack, activity it believes was for reconnaissance and target mapping.
marineinsight
+1

4 sources
Calls for Accountability

Safesea has urged that the investigation be conducted under the oversight of the International Maritime Organization and the United Nations. The company has requested full disclosure of radar data, Automatic Identification System records, and coastal surveillance inputs, raising pointed questions about why Iraqi monitoring systems failed to act on the unusual vessel movements observed before the strike.
marineinsight

In a gesture that underscored the human cost, Anchan traveled on the same flight carrying Singh's remains back to India, accompanied by the vessel's captain. "In shipping, the most important thing is not cargo or cost, but human life," he said.
marineinsight

1 source
Insurance Costs Reshape Gulf Shipping

The attack on the Safesea Vishnu was part of a broader wave of strikes on commercial vessels since the outbreak of hostilities between the U.S., Israel, and Iran. War risk insurance premiums for ships in the Persian Gulf have risen by as much as 1,000 percent or more from pre-conflict levels, according to Reuters, with rates climbing to 2 to 3 percent of a vessel's hull value compared with roughly 0.1 to 0.25 percent before the war. For a tanker valued at $250 million, that translates to a premium of roughly $7.5 million per voyage. S&P Global reported that while premiums eased slightly in late March amid hopes for a diplomatic resolution, they remain up to eight times higher than pre-war levels.

Nepal arrests ex-PM Oli over deadly 2025 protest crackdown

Nepal's former prime minister KP Sharma Oli was arrested on Saturday morning at his residence in Bhaktapur, on the outskirts of Kathmandu, over his alleged role in a deadly crackdown on anti-corruption protesters last September that killed 76 people and led to his ouster. Former home minister Ramesh Lekhak was also detained.

The arrests came just one day after rapper-turned-politician Balendra Shah, 35, was sworn in as Nepal's new prime minister following his Rastriya Swatantra Party's landslide victory in the March 5 parliamentary elections. At Shah's first cabinet meeting on Friday, the government resolved to implement the recommendations of an investigation commission that had called for prosecuting Oli and other officials for their handling of the September 2025 uprising.

+2

Swift Action by New Government

"They were arrested this morning, and the process will move forward according to the law," Kathmandu Valley police spokesperson Om Adhikari told AFP. The 74-year-old Oli was taken from his home in Gundu, Bhaktapur, while Lekhak was arrested at his residence in Suryabinayak around 5 a.m., according to The Kathmandu Post.

+2

New Home Minister Sudan Gurung, who had been a prominent figure in last year's protests, announced the arrests on social media. "No one is above the law," Gurung wrote on Instagram. "This is not revenge against anyone, it is just the beginning of justice".

Both detainees were held at the Kathmandu Police Office and are scheduled to appear before a court on Sunday.

+2

6 sources
Roots in the September 2025 Uprising

The arrests stem from the violent suppression of youth-led protests that erupted on September 8-9, 2025, initially triggered by a government ban on social media platforms. The demonstrations quickly expanded into broader grievances over corruption and economic hardship, with angry mobs setting fire to parliament and government buildings. At least 76 people were killed in two days in what became Nepal's worst violence since the end of its civil war in 2006.
ndtv
+2

An investigation commission established by the interim government of Sushila Karki examined the crackdown and found that while it could not confirm a direct order to open fire, "no attempts were made to halt or manage the firing, and due to their negligence, even minors lost their lives". The commission recommended prosecution under Nepal's criminal code, with potential sentences of up to 10 years.

The party, once a dominant force in Nepalese politics, was reduced to just nine directly elected seats in the March 5 vote, while Shah's RSP secured 182 of the 275 seats in the House of Representatives.

Witnesses reported that Oli, who has undergone two kidney transplants, was transferred to Tribhuvan University Teaching Hospital for a medical examination following his detention.

A Lifeline With Limits

The delivery marked the first crude oil shipment to reach Cuba in nearly three months, offering a temporary reprieve to the country's 10 million residents who have endured rolling blackouts, shuttered hospitals, and disrupted water supplies since the U.S. imposed an informal fuel blockade in late January. The Twenty-Seven Endorse Gibraltar Agreement: To Take Effect July 15

The Twenty-Seven member states of the European Union unanimously backed this Wednesday the signing and provisional application of the agreement between the EU and the United Kingdom that redefines Gibraltar's relationship with the EU bloc and provides for the demolition of the border fence separating La Línea de la Concepción (Cádiz) from the Rock. Provisional application is scheduled for July 15, 2026, three months later than initially planned by Brussels and London, which had set April 10 as the target date.
elpais
+4

The Committee of Permanent Representatives (Coreper) approved the agreement texts and decisions for signature at a meeting of ambassadors in Brussels. According to the Council's statement, the texts will be formally adopted once legal and linguistic reviews are completed, a process that requires at least two months to translate the treaty into all official EU languages.

La aplicación provisional del acuerdo de Gibraltar se retrasa al 15 ...

fernandezrozas
Relaciones UE-Reino Unido: los Estados miembros dan luz verde al ...
bbc.com
A treaty closing the final chapter of Brexit

The agreement, finalized at the political level on June 11, 2025, after more than four years of negotiations between Spain, the United Kingdom, and the European Commission, aims to eliminate "all physical barriers to the movement of people and goods between Spain and Gibraltar, while fully safeguarding the Schengen area, the EU single market, and its customs union," according to the Council. The treaty, which exceeds 1,000 pages with 336 articles and 43 annexes, will complete the legal framework for post-Brexit relations, from which Gibraltar had been excluded since 2021.
democrata
+3

The removal of the Verja, the last physical border wall on continental Europe, will especially benefit the approximately 15,000 cross-border workers who commute daily between both territories. Spain will assume Schengen controls at Gibraltar's airport and port, will have veto power over residence permits, and the final say in issuing short-term visas.
euronews
+2

6 sources
Reactions and Next Steps

Spanish Foreign Minister José Manuel Albares described the agreement as "historic" in a message on social media platform X, celebrating that it provides "certainty for 300,000 Andalusians in the Campo de Gibraltar area," calling it "a success for Spain and for Europe." The Government of Gibraltar also welcomed the unanimous approval by member states.
yourgibraltartv
+2

The treaty still needs to be ratified by the European Parliament and the British Parliament, which has not yet received the final text. In the meantime, provisional application on July 15 will allow the new framework to be implemented before full ratification is completed.

Seizing Iran's uranium by force would risk casualties, experts warn

Should the United States attempt to seize Iran's stockpile of highly enriched uranium by military force, the operation would require as many as 1,000 specially trained troops, carry radiation and chemical hazards, and likely result in casualties, according to experts and former government officials.
military

The warning, detailed in an Associated Press report from Vienna, underscores the tension between President Donald Trump's stated goal that Iran will "never have a nuclear weapon" and the practical difficulties of achieving it on the ground.
military

Published
21 hours ago
military
Securing Iran's Enriched Uranium by Force Would Be Risky and ...
nprillinois
U.S.-Iran nuclear talks wrap up with no announcement of a deal as ...
armscontrolcenter
Iran's Stockpile of Highly Enriched Uranium: Worth Bargaining For?
armscontrol
U.S. Negotiators Were Ill-Prepared for Serious Nuclear Negotiations ...
euronews.com
A Stockpile Shrouded in Uncertainty

Iran possesses 440.9 kilograms of uranium enriched to 60% purity — a short technical step from the 90% weapons-grade threshold — enough for as many as 10 nuclear bombs, according to the International Atomic Energy Agency. IAEA inspectors have not been able to verify the location of the material since June 2025, when joint Israeli and American strikes targeted Iran's nuclear infrastructure.
nprillinois
+2

IAEA Director General Rafael Grossi has said roughly 200 kilograms is believed to be stored in tunnels at a nuclear complex outside Isfahan, with additional quantities at the Natanz and Fordo facilities. U.S. Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard told a House hearing on March 19 that the intelligence community has "high confidence" it knows the stockpile's location.
military

3 sources
Hazmat Suits and Booby Traps

The uranium is stored as hexafluoride gas in canisters weighing about 50 kilograms each. David Albright, a former nuclear weapons inspector and founder of the Institute for Science and International Security, warned that damaged canisters could release fluorine, a highly toxic chemical, and that spacing them improperly during transport risks triggering a critical nuclear reaction.
military

Christine Wormuth, former Army secretary under President Joe Biden and now head of the Nuclear Threat Initiative, called it a "very complex and high risk military operation" that would "probably take casualties." She said the Isfahan site alone could require 1,000 personnel, heavy equipment flown in by helicopter, and possibly a temporary airstrip. Special forces would need to work alongside nuclear experts in tunnels potentially filled with rubble, decoys, and booby traps.
military

"The Iranians have thought this through, I'm sure, and are going to try to make it as difficult as possible," Wormuth said.
military

1 source
The Case for Diplomacy

Experts emphasized that a negotiated settlement remains the safest path. Scott Roecker, a former director at the National Nuclear Security Administration and now a vice president at the Nuclear Threat Initiative, pointed to the 1994 "Project Sapphire" operation, in which the U.S. and Kazakhstan cooperated to secretly remove 600 kilograms of weapons-grade uranium left over from the Soviet program.
military

Grossi said on March 22 that the IAEA is "considering these options, of course," but added: "Nothing can happen while bombs are falling." U.S.-Iran nuclear talks in Geneva in late February ended without a deal, and Trump recently signaled the war could wind down within weeks — leaving the fate of the uranium stockpile as a central unresolved question.

Trump promotes Fox News case for ground troops in Iran

President Donald Trump on Saturday promoted a Fox News broadcast in which host Mark Levin made an extended case for deploying specialized ground forces into Iran to seize the country's stockpile of highly enriched uranium, a move that would mark a dramatic escalation of the month-old U.S.-Iranian conflict just as Secretary of State Marco Rubio insists Washington can achieve its war aims without boots on the ground.

Levin Makes the Case

"Watch Mark Levin interview of Brilliant Marc Thiessen tonight at 8:00 P.M., on FoxNews," Trump wrote on Truth Social on Saturday evening. "Will discuss the importance of hitting Iran, HARD!!!" Hours later, Levin used his program, Life, Liberty & Levin, to argue that U.S. forces must enter Iran to secure as much enriched uranium as possible, warning it could otherwise be fashioned into dirty bombs or advanced missiles. "If it can't be destroyed or modified, we need to retrieve it," Levin said. He stressed that the mission would not require "300,000" soldiers but rather small, specialized units, noting that Trump had discussed deploying elements of the Army's 82nd Airborne Division.
