Marc Thiessen, a Washington Post foreign policy columnist and Fox News contributor, echoed the concern, warning that the easiest form of Iranian retaliation after the war would be to transfer uranium to groups like al-Qaeda for use against Americans.

3 sources
Scale of the Challenge

The idea of a ground operation to seize Iran's nuclear material has been under discussion between U.S. and Israeli officials since early March. Bloomberg first reported that Trump was weighing the deployment of special forces after officials grew concerned that roughly 450 kilograms of uranium enriched to 60 percent purity — enough to produce several nuclear weapons if further enriched — may have been moved from known sites. The Wall Street Journal reported that such a mission could require upward of 1,000 personnel at a single site, including combat troops, engineers with excavation equipment, and nuclear scientists. Retired NATO commander Admiral James Stavridis described the scenario as potentially "the largest special forces operation in history".
bloomberg
+4

IAEA chief Rafael Grossi has said roughly half of the enriched uranium was stored in a tunnel complex at the Isfahan nuclear site, with additional material believed to be at Natanz and Fordow. Forces would likely remain on the ground for days and face drone and missile fire in a hostile environment, with uranium hexafluoride posing severe contamination risks if containers are breached during excavation.

Shell in advanced talks to develop major gas fields in Venezuela

Shell is in advanced negotiations with Venezuela's government to develop four large offshore natural gas areas near Trinidad and Tobago, in what would represent a major expansion of the energy giant's footprint in the country, Reuters reported on Tuesday.
reuters

The talks center on two of South America's largest offshore gas deposits, with combined reserves of roughly 20 trillion cubic feet. Shell is seeking access to three fields that form part of the 12-tcf Mariscal Sucre project off Venezuela's east coast — including the flagship 4.2-tcf Dragon field — as well as the 7.3-tcf Loran offshore field, which straddles the maritime border with Trinidad, according to two people familiar with the discussions.

Dragon and Beyond

LNG Ambitions and Obstacles

Shell plans to pipe Venezuelan gas to Trinidad for processing into liquefied natural gas at the Atlantic LNG facility, in which it holds a 45% stake alongside BP with another 45%. Venezuelan oil exports hit 6-year high as India replaces China

Venezuelan crude oil exports surged to 890,000 barrels per day in March, the highest level since December 2019, as Indian refiners stepped in to fill the gap left by China's retreat from the market, according to Bloomberg. The shift marks a dramatic realignment of Venezuela's oil trade, three months after the Trump administration moved to take control of the country's crude sales.
bloomberg
+1

Venezuela lines up larger oil cargoes as exports to India set to rise
moneycontrol.com
India Steps In as Top Buyer

Shipments to India soared more than fourfold in March, surpassing volumes sent to the United States, Bloomberg reported, citing data from maritime intelligence firm Kpler. The ramp-up followed months of preparation. In February, Reuters reported that trading houses Vitol and Trafigura chartered the first very large crude carriers since the Caracas-Washington supply deal began, with at least three supertankers — Nissos Kea, Nissos Kythnos and Arzanah — assigned March loading slots at Venezuela's José terminal, all bound for India. Indian Oil Corp and Hindustan Petroleum Corp jointly purchased 2 million barrels of Merey crude, while Reliance Industries has been buying Venezuelan oil and exploring direct purchases from PDVSA.
reuters
+3

India's government has also encouraged the buying spree. In February, Bloomberg reported that New Delhi asked refiners to consider purchasing more U.S. and Venezuelan oil as part of broader efforts to diversify away from Russian and Middle Eastern supplies amid geopolitical uncertainty.
bloomberg

5 sources
China's Exit Opens the Door

China, which had averaged roughly 642,000 barrels per day of Venezuelan crude and fuel oil imports in 2025, saw its purchases collapse after Washington's intervention. By February, Venezuelan exports to Asia had plunged 67% to roughly 48,000 barrels per day, according to Reuters, as Chinese buyers pulled back amid narrowing discounts and the risk of U.S. sanctions enforcement. The U.S. seizure of a sanctioned tanker carrying nearly 1.85 million barrels of Merey crude off Venezuela's coast in December further deterred China-bound shipments.
reuters
+2

3 sources
US Oil Majors Keep Their Distance

Despite the export boom, the Trump administration's broader ambition of attracting major U.S. oil companies to invest in Venezuela has gained little traction. At a January White House meeting, Exxon Mobil CEO Darren Woods told President Trump that Venezuela was "uninvestable" without reforms to its legal and commercial frameworks. No firm financial commitments emerged from the meeting, and Trump later suggested he might exclude Exxon from future Venezuelan deals. Chevron, which currently produces about 240,000 barrels per day in the country, has expressed optimism about increasing output over 18 to 24 months but remains the exception among the majors. Venezuela's oil production, including condensate and gas liquids, reached 1.1 million barrels per day in March, according to Reuters.

SpaceX files confidentially for historic IPO targeting $1.75 trillion valuation

SpaceX has confidentially filed its draft IPO registration with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission, Bloomberg News reported on Wednesday, setting the stage for what would be the largest initial public offering ever. The filing, first reported by Bloomberg, keeps Elon Musk's rocket and satellite company on track for a June listing that could raise as much as $75 billion at a valuation of roughly $1.75 trillion.

A Mega-Round Built in Stages

The funding round took shape over several months. OpenAI first announced a $110 billion raise in late February at a $730 billion pre-money valuation, anchored by Amazon with $50 billion, and Nvidia and SoftBank with $30 billion each. The company signaled at the time that additional investors were expected to join.

+1

Shaw Ventures, MGX, TPG, and T. Rowe Price, pushing the total past $120 billion. Microsoft, a longtime investor and computing partner, also participated. French President Emmanuel Macron used a visit to Tokyo on Wednesday to deliver a pointed critique of the Trump administration's handling of the Iran conflict, warning that a hasty American withdrawal from the Middle East without a diplomatic framework in place would amount to a worst-case scenario.

"Nothing Worse Than Bombing and Pulling Back"

In an interview with Japanese television while in Tokyo, Macron cautioned that a U.S. departure without a deal with Iran could carry severe consequences. "There is nothing worse than conducting airstrikes in the area for weeks and then departing without creating a new framework," he said, according to The Wall Street Journal. The remarks came as President Donald Trump signaled that the U.S. military could end its offensive against Iran within "two to three weeks" and suggested leaving it to other countries to resolve issues with the Strait of Hormuz.
dw
youtube
The Wall Street Journal

Macron also praised Europe's "predictability" in a speech to business leaders and investors, drawing an implicit contrast with Washington. "Predictability has value, and we have demonstrated it over the past years, and even in the past weeks: we are where you know we will be," he said. "That is not bad in these times, believe me."
anews

The exchange followed Trump's criticism of France on Truth Social on Tuesday, in which he called Paris "very unhelpful" in the Iran conflict and alleged it had blocked military planes headed to Israel.

Japan's Energy Vulnerability at the Center

Macron's host, Japanese Prime Minister Sanae Takaichi, shares deep concerns over the crisis. Japan relies on the Middle East for more than 90 percent of its crude oil imports, and the Strait of Hormuz — through which roughly 20 million barrels of oil normally pass daily — has been effectively blockaded since the U.S. and Israel launched strikes on Iran on February 28.
aljazeera
+1

After their bilateral talks, the two leaders issued a joint call for "a return to peace, a ceasefire, calm, and free passage through the Strait of Hormuz," according to the Associated Press. Iran has allowed limited vessel transits, selectively granting passage to countries it does not consider adversaries, including China, India, and potentially Japan.

Diplomacy Versus Force

The French president has consistently argued that airstrikes alone cannot resolve the conflict. In a March interview aboard the aircraft carrier Charles de Gaulle, he said, "I don't believe we can instigate significant transformations in a regime or political structure solely through bombing". France has also stated it would not participate in military operations to forcibly reopen the Strait while hostilities continue.

In a memo to employees in March, Suleyman wrote that he would devote all his energy to delivering "world class models for Microsoft over the next five years".

+1

16 minutes ago
moneycontrol
Microsoft AI chief signals plan to move beyond OpenAI as it builds its ...
cnbc
Microsoft AI chief sees benefits to AI models that are months behind
fortune
Microsoft AI chief gives it 18 months—for all white-collar work to be ...
+114 sources
cnbc.com
From 'Off-Frontier' to the Frontier

Microsoft's in-house model development has evolved rapidly. As recently as April 2025, Suleyman described the company's approach as deliberately operating "off-frontier" — training models three to six months behind the leading edge to save costs and avoid duplication. At the time, he called it "more economical" to let rivals push the boundary first.
cnbc

That posture has shifted. In a February 2026 interview with the Financial Times, Suleyman declared that Microsoft must "develop our own foundation models which are at the absolute frontier, with gigawatt-scale compute and some of the very best AI training teams in the world". The company has since launched several homegrown models, including MAI-1-preview for text, MAI-Voice-1 for speech, and MAI-Image-2, which Microsoft says ranks among the top three text-to-image systems globally.
moneycontrol
+3

5 sources
The Compute Challenge

A key constraint has been raw computing power. Microsoft's first in-house foundation model, MAI-1-preview, was trained on roughly 15,000 Nvidia H100 GPUs — a fraction of the resources competitors deploy. Suleyman told employees in a September 2025 town hall that the company would make "significant investments" in its own chip clusters, aspiring to train on infrastructure "six to ten times larger" than its initial efforts.
theverge
+2

Microsoft's custom Maia 200 AI chip, designed for cost-efficient inference, is part of a broader "silicon to service" strategy, with a next-generation Maia 300 chip expected around 2027. The company's capital expenditure on AI infrastructure has exceeded $120 billion in fiscal year 2026.
businessengineer
+1

5 sources
A Multi-Model Future

Despite the drive toward self-sufficiency, Microsoft has stressed it is not abandoning its partnership with OpenAI, whose models it can access through 2032. Communications chief Frank X. Shaw has said Microsoft sees itself operating in a "multi-model world," supplementing its own systems with offerings from OpenAI, Anthropic, and others. Suleyman recently argued on X that the next two to three years of AI competition will be defined less by who builds the smartest model and more by who can afford to run models at scale.
timesofindia.indiatimes
+4

The 2027 frontier target would mark a turning point for a company that has spent billions backing external AI partners — and now intends to stand alongside them.

OpenAI's Brockman says GPT models have 'line of sight' to AGI

OpenAI President Greg Brockman declared that the long-running debate over whether large language models can achieve artificial general intelligence has been settled. Speaking on the Big Technology Podcast in an episode published on Tuesday, Brockman said OpenAI now sees a direct path from its GPT reasoning models to AGI.

"There's been this debate of how far will the text models go? How far can text intelligence go?" Brockman said. "And I think that we have definitively answered that question. It is going to go to AGI. Like, we see line of sight."

The 'Spud' Model

Brockman also offered a detailed preview of an upcoming flagship model internally codenamed "Spud," which he described as the product of nearly two years of research. Unlike incremental updates, Spud will serve as an entirely new base model underpinning all future OpenAI models, he said.
thehansindia
+1

"I think it's going to be able to solve both much harder problems. I think it will be much more nuanced. It'll understand instructions better. It'll understand the context much better," Brockman told the podcast. He introduced the phrase "big model smell" to describe the qualitative leap users would feel when interacting with a model that is substantively more capable, suggesting that Spud would reduce the frustration of having to repeatedly clarify instructions to an AI system.

OpenClaw becomes gateway for Chinese AI services globally

The open-source AI agent OpenClaw has become the primary channel through which Chinese artificial intelligence services are reaching global users, reshaping the competitive landscape of the AI industry. Bloomberg reported on Wednesday that the platform now handles token processing for dozens of Chinese AI providers, making affordable models from firms like MiniMax and Moonshot accessible to developers worldwide through familiar APIs.
bloomberg
+1

Published
23 minutes ago
caliber
China gains edge in AI race through token pricing power - Caliber.Az
ft
The rise of China's hottest new commodity: AI tokens - Financial Times
indexbox
Chinese AI Models Lead Global Token Usage Ranking in 2026
reuters
Chinese tech hubs promote OpenClaw AI agent despite ... - Reuters
turkiyetoday.com
A Pricing Edge That Compounds With Scale

The economic implications are stark. Chinese AI labs including MiniMax and Moonshot charge roughly $2 to $3 per million output tokens, compared with about $15 for comparable Western models such as Anthropic's Claude Sonnet, according to an analysis by the Financial Times. That roughly fivefold to sixfold cost advantage becomes especially potent in the era of AI agents, which consume far more tokens than traditional chatbots. While a chatbot might use around 30,000 tokens to summarize a text, an AI agent can burn through up to 20 million tokens for a modest coding task.
caliber
+1

"Even small price differences become critical when AI agents burn through millions of tokens a day," noted AI analyst Will Liang, as quoted by the Financial Times. One developer cited in the FT report cut projected daily costs from $900 to about $50 by switching primarily to Moonshot's Kimi model.
caliber

Data from OpenRouter shows that Chinese open-source models led by MiniMax's M2.5 and Moonshot's Kimi K2.5 have overtaken American rivals in global token consumption since February, with the three largest Chinese providers — MiniMax, Moonshot, and DeepSeek — accounting for nearly two-thirds of token usage among the platform's top five models.
indexbox

3 sources
OpenClaw as the Distribution Layer

OpenClaw, created by Austrian developer Peter Steinberger and released on GitHub in November 2025, is not itself an AI model but an open-source "agentic harness" that runs locally on a user's device and connects to any large language model via API. Its model-agnostic design made it a natural distribution vehicle for Chinese AI services seeking overseas adoption. In early 2026, OpenClaw added free support for Moonshot's Kimi K2.5 and MiniMax models, citing their cost efficiency.
reuters
+2

The tool has found its most enthusiastic user base in China, where Tencent integrated it into WeChat, and local governments in Shenzhen have offered subsidies for businesses building on it. A Bloomberg video report noted that China now has nearly double the OpenClaw activity of the United States, according to cybersecurity firm SecurityScorecard.
cnbc
youtube
reuters

5 sources
Risks and Limits

The expansion is not without friction. Chinese authorities have restricted state agencies from installing OpenClaw, citing cybersecurity vulnerabilities including prompt injection attacks and data leaks. Infrastructure strain has also emerged — Zhipu AI faced service disruptions after a surge in demand for its GLM-5 model. And geopolitical wariness over Chinese-hosted AI infrastructure remains a barrier for governments and regulated industries in the West.
nytimes
+2

Still, as Bloomberg's Tim Culpan wrote this week, the OpenClaw phenomenon offers China's AI sector "a reason to charge more for tokens" while providing the messy, real-world training data that can accelerate the broader ecosystem.
bloomberg

4 sources
Discover more

The tool's rapid spread has not come without worry. Chinese cybersecurity authorities and Beijing's IT ministry have issued warnings about data risks posed by giving AI agents access to personal information. Steinberger, who was hired by OpenAI in February to lead its next generation of personal agents, acknowledged the tension. "If you build a hammer, you can hurt yourself. So should we not...

Investors can't unload OpenAI shares as Anthropic demand surges

OpenAI shares have become nearly impossible to sell on secondary markets, as institutional investors rapidly pivot toward rival Anthropic in a striking reversal of sentiment in the private AI market.

About six institutional investors — including hedge funds and venture capital firms holding large stakes — have approached Next Round Capital in recent weeks looking to offload approximately $600 million worth of OpenAI equity, but the firm has found no buyers, according to Bloomberg. "We simply can't find any institutional investors willing to take these shares, and we have access to hundreds of institutions," Next Round Capital founder Ken Smythe said. A year ago, such offerings would have been snapped up within days.
thedeepdive

bloomberg.com
Anthropic Draws Record Demand

The contrast with Anthropic could not be sharper. Secondary market platforms including Augment, Hiive, and Next Round Capital report bids valuing Anthropic at roughly $600 billion — more than 50% above its last funding round valuation of $380 billion. On the Hiive platform alone, demand for Anthropic shares has exceeded $1.6 billion, while roughly $2 billion in buyer capital is lined up across platforms waiting to acquire Anthropic equity.
news.futunn
+2

Adam Crawley, co-founder of Augment, pointed to the gap between OpenAI's $852 billion valuation and Anthropic's $380 billion as the central driver. "People are betting that Anthropic's valuation will catch up with OpenAI's," Crawley told Bloomberg. "And if you buy OpenAI shares now, the short-term profit prospects aren't as clear". Meanwhile, OpenAI shares are being bid at roughly $765 billion — a 10% discount from its prior $850 billion level.
thedeepdive
+1

4 sources
Enterprise Growth Fuels the Shift

Underlying the market dynamics is Anthropic's accelerating revenue trajectory. The company recently surpassed $19 billion in annualized run-rate revenue, more than doubling from $9 billion at the end of 2025, driven by strong enterprise adoption of its Claude AI models and coding tools, Bloomberg reported in March. Some analysts project Anthropic could overtake OpenAI in revenue by mid-2026.
epochai.substack
+1

OpenAI, by contrast, faces mounting questions about its cost structure. The company is projected to lose approximately $14 billion in 2026, driven by soaring compute and infrastructure expenses, even as it recently closed a record $122 billion fundraising round. Both companies officially prohibit unauthorized secondary trading of their shares, though investors circumvent restrictions through special purpose vehicles and other channels. An OpenAI spokesperson cautioned that "people should exercise extreme caution toward any company claiming it can provide access to OpenAI shares".

OpenAI CFO says company is turning down work over compute shortage

The two most prominent AI startups in the world are running up against the same wall: there is not enough computing power to meet the explosive demand for their products. In interviews released this week, top OpenAI executives painted a stark picture of the constraints now shaping the company's strategy, while Anthropic has been forced to throttle its own paying customers as usage overwhelms capacity.

Published
2 hours ago
africa.businessinsider
OpenAI's CFO says the company is passing on opportunities ...
techcrunch
Why OpenAI really shut down Sora - TechCrunch
wsj
OpenAI Scraps Sora Video Platform Months After Launch - WSJ
podscripts
Big Technology Podcast - OpenAI President Greg Brockman: AI Self ...
siliconrepublic.com
OpenAI Makes "Very Painful Decisions"

OpenAI CFO Sarah Friar told ARK Invest CEO Cathie Wood in an interview released this week that the company is actively turning away business. "We're making some very tough trades at the moment and things we're not pursuing because we don't have enough compute," Friar said, adding that she spends much of her time "trying to find any last-minute compute available here in 2026." "If you do not have it, you do not have revenue. That is one thing I know for sure," she said.
africa.businessinsider

OpenAI President Greg Brockman reinforced that message on the Big Technology Podcast, released on March 31. "We cannot build compute fast enough to keep up with demand," Brockman said, describing "very painful decisions" about what to launch and where to allocate resources. The pressure has already forced product cuts. On March 24, OpenAI announced it would discontinue its Sora video generation tool, launched just last year, to redirect computing resources and talent toward core revenue-generating products like its coding tools and planned "superapp." According to The Wall Street Journal, the entertainment giant Disney, which had committed $1 billion to a Sora partnership, learned of the shutdown less than an hour before the public announcement.
techcrunch
+3

4 sources
Anthropic Feels the Squeeze

Anthropic is facing a parallel crunch. Late last month, the company adjusted usage limits for Claude subscribers across all tiers, warning that users would hit their session caps faster during peak hours — defined as 5 a.m. to 11 a.m. Pacific Time — even as weekly limits remain unchanged. A member of Anthropic's technical staff posted on X that roughly seven percent of users would "hit session limits they wouldn't have before." The company also offered a temporary promotion doubling usage during off-peak hours, an implicit acknowledgment of strained infrastructure.
theaieconomy.substack
+2

Claude has also suffered outages. On March 2, a worldwide disruption left thousands of users unable to access Claude.ai and Claude Code, according to Anthropic's status page and TechCrunch. One industry analyst noted that Anthropic's uptime fell to "one nine" at points during the month, and argued the company was "actively degrading" its products to free up compute.
bleepingcomputer
+2

6 sources
An Industry-Wide Reckoning

The compute crunch carries broader implications. CEO Dario Amodei warned in a February interview that the stakes of miscalculating infrastructure investment are existential. "If my revenue is not $1 trillion, if it's even $800 billion, there's no force on Earth, there's no hedge on Earth that could stop me from going bankrupt if I buy that much compute," he said, defending a more cautious spending approach compared to hyperscalers. Anthropic's revenue has climbed to nearly $10 billion annually, according to Amodei, but the gap between what customers want and what the company can serve continues to widen.
linkedin
+2

OpenAI, meanwhile, recently secured an additional $10 billion in funding, bringing its total raise above $120 billion, as it prepares for a potential IPO later this year. Yet for both companies, the constraint is not capital or ambition — it is the physical hardware to turn either into products.
cnbc

4 sources

Open-source rewrite of leaked Claude Code hits 72,000 GitHub stars

An open-source AI coding agent framework called Claw Code has rocketed to more than 72,000 GitHub stars and 72,600 forks within days of its public launch, establishing itself as one of the fastest-growing repositories in the AI tooling space. The project, built in Python and Rust, emerged directly from one of the most talked-about incidents in the AI industry this year: Anthropic's accidental leak of the entire Claude Code source code on March 31.
ndtv
+3

Published
1 hour ago
wavespeed
What Is claw-code? The Claude Code Rewrite Explained
ndtv
"2026 Just Got Crazy": Internet Erupts After Anthropic Source Code Leak Shakes AI Industry
linas.substack
Anthropic accidentally leaked Claude Code's entire source. Here's ...
+25 sources
arstechnica.com
From Leak to Rewrite in Hours

On the morning of March 31, 2026, security researcher Chaofan Shou confirmed that Anthropic had inadvertently shipped a 60MB source-map file inside a Claude Code npm update, exposing roughly 512,000 lines of TypeScript across some 1,900 files. The leak revealed Claude Code's internal architecture, unreleased feature flags, and tooling — though not model weights or user data. Anthropic confirmed the incident was "a release packaging issue caused by human error, not a security breach".
linas.substack
+3

As mirrors of the leaked code spread and Anthropic filed DMCA takedowns to pull them from GitHub, Korean developer Sigrid Jin — known online as @instructkr and @sigridjineth — took a different path. Rather than simply archiving the proprietary TypeScript, Jin sat down and rewrote the core architecture from scratch in Python before sunrise, using OpenAI's Codex as an orchestration layer. The resulting repository, claw-code, hit 50,000 stars in roughly two hours, one of the fastest accumulation rates GitHub has recorded.
wavespeed
+1

5 sources
What Claw Code Actually Is

Claw Code is not a copy of Claude Code. It is a clean-room rewrite that reimplements core architectural patterns — including the tool system, query engine, multi-agent orchestration, and memory management — without incorporating any of Anthropic's proprietary source. Each capability, from file reading to Git operations, is implemented as a self-contained tool with granular permission controls.
claw-code
+1

The project addresses what its creators describe as a structural gap in the AI ecosystem: while large language models have advanced rapidly, the "agent harness" layer connecting them to tools, file systems, and workflows has remained largely proprietary. Claw Code aims to provide an open, auditable alternative that developers can study and extend.
markets.financialcontent

2 sources
Legal Questions and Limitations

The legal logic behind the project rests on its clean-room methodology — no original TypeScript was ported — but unresolved intellectual property questions remain. According to an analysis by WaveSpeed AI, Claw Code is not yet at feature parity with Claude Code, the Rust port is not stable, and for production coding work, Anthropic's official tool remains the more complete option. Jin himself has been candid about the project's limitations, with a friend noting on X that "he built claw-code and is the first to call it a demo".
x
+1

Claude Code leak reveals hidden telemetry and remote killswitches

When Anthropic accidentally shipped the entire source code of its AI coding assistant Claude Code last week, the immediate headlines focused on the embarrassment of a safety-focused company making a basic packaging error. But as security researchers and journalists have dug through the 512,000 lines of exposed TypeScript, a more consequential picture has emerged: Claude Code exercises far more control over users' machines — and communicates far more data back to Anthropic — than most developers likely realized.

Published
Apr 1, 2026
modemguides
Claude Code Source Code Leaked via npm: What You Need to Know
fortune
Anthropic mistakenly leaks its own AI coding tool's source ... - Fortune
cnbc
Anthropic leaks part of Claude Code's internal source code - CNBC
gizmodo
Source Code for Anthropic’s Claude Code Leaks at the Exact Wrong Time
cnbc.com
What the Code Reveals

The leak, which occurred on March 31 after a source map file was mistakenly bundled into Claude Code version 2.1.88 on npm, was first spotted by security researcher Chaofan Shou, whose post on X drew tens of millions of views. Anthropic confirmed the exposure was caused by "human error, not a security breach," and said no customer data or credentials were involved.
thehackernews
+3

But the exposed codebase — roughly 1,900 TypeScript files now permanently mirrored across public GitHub repositories — tells a detailed story about what happens on a developer's machine when Claude Code is running. The Register reported that the code shows how much information Anthropic can collect about users and their systems. Every file Claude reads, every bash command it executes, and every edit it makes is logged locally in plaintext JSONL files, with session transcripts referenced throughout the codebase's memory and "dream" consolidation systems. According to a comparison by DevCompare, Anthropic retains this data for up to five years for consumer users who have the "Help improve Claude" setting enabled.
fortune
+5

The code also reveals persistent telemetry that polls Anthropic's servers every hour and can push configuration changes to running instances via feature flags — without requiring a user-initiated update. Six or more remote killswitches can force behaviors including bypassing permission prompts, toggling analytics, and in some cases forcing the application to exit entirely. An auto-update mechanism allows Anthropic to remotely enable or disable specific versions.
modemguides

10 sources
Hidden Features and Internal Tools

Among 44 unreleased feature flags, researchers found an internal-only tool called "DiscoverSkills" — an AI-powered skill search available exclusively to Anthropic employees. The tool list also revealed KAIROS, a persistent autonomous agent mode that can proactively initiate actions and consolidate its own memory while a user is idle, and an "Undercover Mode" that instructs Claude to hide all evidence of AI involvement when Anthropic employees use the tool to contribute to open-source projects.
kuber
+3

The leak is Anthropic's second data exposure in five days. Fortune had reported days earlier that a misconfigured content management system exposed details about an unreleased model codenamed "Mythos," along with roughly 3,000 unpublished internal files.
fortune

5 sources
What It Means for Developers

The revelations arrive as Claude Code has become one of the most widely adopted AI coding tools in the industry, with Anthropic preparing for a potential initial public offering. For developers running Claude Code on sensitive projects, the exposed architecture confirms that the tool maintains what one analysis described as "a persistent remote control channel to Anthropic's servers" — context that matters for anyone granting it filesystem access and terminal execution privileges on their development machines.
gizmodo
+1

Anthropic has patched the npm package and deleted earlier versions from the registry, but the code remains permanently accessible through forks and mirrors.
theregister
+1

Feature branch throughput has surged nearly 50% among top...

Top astronomer warns Artemis program risks 'interplanetary Wild West'

Hours after NASA successfully launched four astronauts toward the moon on the Artemis II mission on Tuesday, the president of the Royal Astronomical Society cautioned that the broader Artemis program risks enabling unchecked commercial exploitation of space without adequate international oversight.

Published
1 hour ago
reading
Artemis mission cannot lead to interplanetary Wild West
blogs.loc
How the Antarctic Treaty of 1959 Influenced the Outer Space Treaty ...
phys
Moon mining is getting closer to reality: Why we need global rules ...
+27 sources
timesofisrael.com
A Call for Restraint

Professor Mike Lockwood, a space environment physicist at the University of Reading and head of Britain's leading astronomical body, said in a statement that discussion of lunar mining under the Artemis umbrella could run afoul of existing international law.
reading

"The commercialisation of Artemis II is mainly in the form of the services supplied to support the mission, but there is talk about the Artemis programme paving the way for mining of the moon," Lockwood said. "This would be contrary to international law".
reading

He pointed to the 1967 Outer Space Treaty, which states that no nation or company can claim ownership of a celestial body or contaminate it. "We do not want a frontier mentality and a lack of sustainable thinking to produce an interplanetary Wild West," he warned.
blogs.loc
+1

2 sources
Geopolitics and a New Treaty

Lockwood noted that while the Artemis program is an international collaboration — more than 60 nations have signed the U.S.-led Artemis Accords — it notably excludes China and Russia. That omission, he argued, undercuts the program's potential to serve as a foundation for broader cooperation.
phys
+1

He called for a new international space treaty modeled on the Antarctic Treaty, which entered into force in 1961 to ban territorial claims and military activity on the continent. "It is now 50 years since the first exploration of the moon but the world today is not in such a cooperative mood, so a similar treaty may be more difficult to agree," Lockwood said.
reading
+1

3 sources
The Legal Gray Zone

The legal debate is not new but has grown more urgent. The Artemis Accords assert that extracting space resources "does not inherently constitute national appropriation" under the Outer Space Treaty. Critics, however, argue this interpretation stretches the treaty's intent, effectively allowing nations to establish exclusion zones on the lunar surface that amount to territorial claims by another name.
theverge
+2

Artemis II, which launched at 6:35 p.m. EDT on April 1 from Kennedy Space Center, is carrying astronauts Reid Wiseman, Victor Glover, Christina Koch, and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen on a 10-day trip around the moon. The mission is the first crewed voyage beyond low Earth orbit since Apollo 17 in 1972 and is intended to test systems for eventual lunar landings under Artemis IV, projected for 2028.
space
+3

Q1 venture funding hit $300B as AI coding tools drew billions

The first quarter of 2026 cemented AI-powered coding tools as one of the most aggressively funded categories in venture capital, with billions of dollars flowing into startups building autonomous coding agents, AI-assisted development environments, and security platforms for AI-generated code. The surge came as part of a record-shattering quarter for global startup investment, which hit $297 billion according to Crunchbase data — with roughly 80% directed at AI companies.
news.crunchbase
+1

Published
2 hours ago
bloomberg
AI Coding Startup Cursor in Talks for About $50 Billion Valuation
techcrunch
Cursor has reportedly surpassed $2B in annualized revenue
linkedin
Cursor AI Seeks $50B Funding Round, Doubles Revenue to $2B
+84 sources
cnbc.com
A Market Moving at Breakneck Speed

At the center of the boom is Cursor, the AI coding assistant built by Anysphere, which Bloomberg reported in March is in talks for a new funding round that could value the company at roughly $50 billion — nearly double its $29.3 billion valuation from a $2.3 billion raise in November 2025. The startup's annualized revenue doubled to $2 billion over just three months, with enterprise customers now accounting for about 60% of sales, Bloomberg reported.
bloomberg
+3

Cursor is far from alone. Cognition AI, maker of the autonomous coding agent Devin, raised $400 million at a $10.2 billion valuation in September 2025 after acquiring Windsurf's team, consolidating its position in autonomous software engineering. Paris-based Poolside, which builds AI models for software development, was raising a $2 billion round at a $12 billion valuation in late 2025, backed by Nvidia with a commitment of up to $1 billion. And by mid-February 2026, TechCrunch reported that at least 17 U.S.-based AI startups had already closed mega-rounds exceeding $100 million each.
techcrunch
+4

9 sources
Competition and Consolidation Intensify

The flood of capital has intensified competition among incumbents and newcomers alike. GitHub Copilot, Anthropic's Claude Code, and OpenAI's Codex are all vying for developer adoption alongside venture-backed challengers like Augment Code, which has raised $252 million to date. OpenAI's completed $3 billion acquisition of Windsurf in 2025 signaled that foundational model companies view coding tools as a strategic priority.
texau
+2

Security is also emerging as a distinct investment thesis. Snyk launched its Agent Security platform at RSA Conference 2026 in late March, designed to govern autonomous coding agents like Cursor, Claude Code, and Devin as enterprises deploy them at scale.
snyk

4 sources
Investor Confidence Meets Market Questions

Despite concerns about market saturation — Gartner has predicted that over 40% of autonomous AI initiatives could be abandoned by the end of 2027 due to rising costs and unclear business value — investors appear undeterred. Developer tools and autonomous coding companies command revenue multiples of 26x to 35x, with outliers far higher, according to an analysis by Finro. As Cursor's trajectory illustrates, the category's combination of rapid revenue growth and deep enterprise adoption continues to justify premium valuations in a market where AI captures the vast majority of venture dollars.

IRENA: Asia drove record renewable growth in 2025 amid war-fueled energy crisis

The war between the United States and Iran is reshaping energy policy across Asia, as governments confront the fragility of fossil fuel supply chains and look to renewables as a path toward energy security. With the Strait of Hormuz — a chokepoint for roughly 20 percent of the world's oil and liquefied natural gas trade — disrupted by the conflict, Asian economies that depend heavily on imported hydrocarbons are facing soaring costs, supply shortages, and mounting pressure to diversify.
eco-business
+1

Published
2 hours ago
eco-business
Renewables shift needed as Iran war exposes Asia's fragile energy ...
gasoutlook
Pakistani solar boom is shielding it from the Hormuz crisis: new report
energytracker
Solar Power Shields Pakistan From the Hormuz Energy Crisis
secureenergyproject
The hedge that paid off: How Pakistan's solar boom is shielding it ...
zawya.com
A Solar Success Story in Pakistan

Pakistan has emerged as an unlikely model for how rapid renewable adoption can cushion an economy from geopolitical shocks. A joint report by the Centre for Research on Energy and Clean Air and Renewables First found that the country's solar transition has allowed it to avoid more than $12 billion in oil and gas imports between 2021 and early 2026. Pakistan grew from under 1 GW of solar PV imports in 2018 to over 51 GW by early 2026, one of the fastest consumer-led energy transitions on record, driving a 40 percent drop in oil and gas imports between 2022 and 2024. Solar is now expected to supply 20 percent of the country's electricity by the end of this year. As rooftop panels have spread across homes, farms, and factories, demand for LNG has fallen, and some long-term LNG contracts have been renegotiated or diverted to international markets.
gasoutlook
+2

3 sources
Regional Leaders Sound the Alarm

South Korean President Lee Jae Myung on Monday called for a rapid shift to renewable energy, warning that continued dependence on fossil fuels leaves the country exposed to recurring geopolitical risk. "This latest war in the Middle East has made it clear that the energy transition, that is the major shift to renewable energy, is no longer a national and historical task that can be postponed," Lee said, according to the Chosun Ilbo and other outlets. In Indonesia, President Prabowo Subianto has appointed Energy Minister Bahlil Lahadalia to lead a task force aimed at accelerating the country's clean energy transition, with expansion of solar, geothermal, and biodiesel among the government's priorities. Indonesia's renewable energy share currently stands at 15.75 percent, with a new target of reaching 17 to 21 percent by the end of 2026.
chosun
+5

6 sources
Structural Barriers Remain

Yet the path forward is uneven. Coal consumption in Southeast Asia is rising faster than anywhere else in the world, according to the International Energy Agency, with demand projected to increase by over 4 percent annually through the end of the decade. Vietnam imported a record 65 million metric tonnes of coal in 2025, and long-term power purchase agreements in Vietnam, Thailand, and the Philippines continue to pose barriers to early coal retirement. Climate advocates meeting in Kuala Lumpur last week warned that high gas prices could give governments cover to extend the lifespan of coal plants. "Coal expansion has really slowed down in Southeast Asia. But because of these high prices, we are afraid that they're going to lift the ban on expansion," said Lidy Nacpil of the Asian Peoples' Movement on Debt and Development.
seattletimes
+2

A new report from the International Renewable Energy Agency, released on Wednesday, offered a counterpoint: global renewable energy capacity jumped by 692 GW in 2025, reaching 5,149 GW, with Asia contributing 74.2 percent of all new additions. Solar alone accounted for 511 GW, or about 75 percent of the total growth. The numbers reinforce the economic logic of renewables — but as the crisis deepens, the question is whether Asia's most coal-dependent nations can move fast enough.
solarquarter
+1

Germany rushed to build LNG terminals to replace Russian gas, while broader energy transition efforts stalled, according to Pauline Heinrichs, a climate and energy...] (https://www.perplexity.ai/discover/tech/iran-war-drives-global-surge-i-kL_VD2hKQumFqGQE7smkuQ)

Across Southeast Asia, governments are both expanding coal use and accelerating clean energy investment. South Korea has lifted restrictions on coal-fired generation, while Indonesia, Thailand, the Philippines, and Vietnam have all boosted coal output to compensate for LNG shortages, according to the Associated Press. Yet the crisis is simultaneously strengthening the case for renewables — a...] (https://www.perplexity.ai/discover/tech/trump-delays-iran-attack-threa-IKnkp_nKRvybqpnh0ROx1Q)

OpenAI CFO says company is turning down work over compute shortage

The two most prominent AI startups in the world are running up against the same wall: there is not enough computing power to meet the explosive demand for their products. In interviews released this week, top OpenAI executives painted a stark picture of the constraints now shaping the company's strategy, while Anthropic has been forced to throttle its own paying customers as usage overwhelms capacity.

Published
2 hours ago
africa.businessinsider
OpenAI's CFO says the company is passing on opportunities ...
techcrunch
Why OpenAI really shut down Sora - TechCrunch
wsj
OpenAI Scraps Sora Video Platform Months After Launch - WSJ
podscripts
Big Technology Podcast - OpenAI President Greg Brockman: AI Self ...
siliconrepublic.com
OpenAI Makes "Very Painful Decisions"

OpenAI CFO Sarah Friar told ARK Invest CEO Cathie Wood in an interview released this week that the company is actively turning away business. "We're making some very tough trades at the moment and things we're not pursuing because we don't have enough compute," Friar said, adding that she spends much of her time "trying to find any last-minute compute available here in 2026." "If you do not have it, you do not have revenue. That is one thing I know for sure," she said.
africa.businessinsider

OpenAI President Greg Brockman reinforced that message on the Big Technology Podcast, released on March 31. "We cannot build compute fast enough to keep up with demand," Brockman said, describing "very painful decisions" about what to launch and where to allocate resources. The pressure has already forced product cuts. On March 24, OpenAI announced it would discontinue its Sora video generation tool, launched just last year, to redirect computing resources and talent toward core revenue-generating products like its coding tools and planned "superapp." According to The Wall Street Journal, the entertainment giant Disney, which had committed $1 billion to a Sora partnership, learned of the shutdown less than an hour before the public announcement.
techcrunch
+3

4 sources
Anthropic Feels the Squeeze

Anthropic is facing a parallel crunch. Late last month, the company adjusted usage limits for Claude subscribers across all tiers, warning that users would hit their session caps faster during peak hours — defined as 5 a.m. to 11 a.m. Pacific Time — even as weekly limits remain unchanged. A member of Anthropic's technical staff posted on X that roughly seven percent of users would "hit session limits they wouldn't have before." The company also offered a temporary promotion doubling usage during off-peak hours, an implicit acknowledgment of strained infrastructure.
theaieconomy.substack
+2

Claude has also suffered outages. On March 2, a worldwide disruption left thousands of users unable to access Claude.ai and Claude Code, according to Anthropic's status page and TechCrunch. One industry analyst noted that Anthropic's uptime fell to "one nine" at points during the month, and argued the company was "actively degrading" its products to free up compute.
bleepingcomputer
+2

6 sources
An Industry-Wide Reckoning

The compute crunch carries broader implications. CEO Dario Amodei warned in a February interview that the stakes of miscalculating infrastructure investment are existential. "If my revenue is not $1 trillion, if it's even $800 billion, there's no force on Earth, there's no hedge on Earth that could stop me from going bankrupt if I buy that much compute," he said, defending a more cautious spending approach compared to hyperscalers. Anthropic's revenue has climbed to nearly $10 billion annually, according to Amodei, but the gap between what customers want and what the company can serve continues to widen.
linkedin
+2

OpenAI, meanwhile, recently secured an additional $10 billion in funding, bringing its total raise above $120 billion, as it prepares for a potential IPO later this year. Yet for both companies, the constraint is not capital or ambition — it is the physical hardware to turn either into products.
cnbc

4 sources

OpenAI's Brockman says GPT models have 'line of sight' to AGI

OpenAI President Greg Brockman declared that the long-running debate over whether large language models can achieve artificial general intelligence has been settled. Speaking on the Big Technology Podcast in an episode published on Tuesday, Brockman said OpenAI now sees a direct path from its GPT reasoning models to AGI.

"There's been this debate of how far will the text models go? How far can text intelligence go?" Brockman said. "And I think that we have definitively answered that question. It is going to go to AGI. Like, we see line of sight."
youtube
thehansindia

2 hours ago
thehansindia
OpenAI's 'Spud' Model Could Mark a Major Leap Toward AGI

OpenAI President Greg Brockman: AI Self-Improvement ... - YouTube

myind.net
The 'Spud' Model

Brockman also offered a detailed preview of an upcoming flagship model internally codenamed "Spud," which he described as the product of nearly two years of research. Unlike incremental updates, Spud will serve as an entirely new base model underpinning all future OpenAI models, he said.
thehansindia
+1

"I think it's going to be able to solve both much harder problems. I think it will be much more nuanced. It'll understand instructions better. It'll understand the context much better," Brockman told the podcast. He introduced the phrase "big model smell" to describe the qualitative leap users would feel when interacting with a model that is substantively more capable, suggesting that Spud would reduce the frustration of having to repeatedly clarify instructions to an AI system.
ndtvprofit
+1

OpenAI CEO Sam Altman had previously told staff that the model, which was trained at the Stargate facility in Abilene, Texas using over 100,000 H100 GPUs made by Nvidia, is "very strong" and could "really accelerate the economy."

instagram

4 sources
Why OpenAI Killed Sora

The AGI push comes as OpenAI shuttered its video-generation app Sora last week, a move that abruptly ended a $1 billion partnership with Disney. Brockman framed the decision as a matter of strategic focus, saying OpenAI chose to bet on its GPT reasoning model architecture over video generation. The company said it needed to redirect scarce computing resources toward its AI agent goals and enterprise products as it races to achieve profitability.
techcrunch
+1
youtube

According to a report by The Wall Street Journal, OpenAI's CEO of applications Fidji Simo had told staff at an all-hands meeting that the company would be dropping "side quests" to concentrate on AI-generated coding and growing its enterprise business. Brockman added that the applications OpenAI has "always dreamed of are starting to come into reach," and that AGI could emerge within the next few years.

Artemis II crew fixes toilet glitch after historic moon launch

Hours after NASA launched four astronauts toward the moon on the first crewed lunar voyage in more than half a century, the Artemis II crew faced a decidedly unglamorous problem: a broken toilet.

Mission specialist Christina Koch reported a jammed fan in the Orion spacecraft's Universal Waste Management System during life support checks on Wednesday evening, telling Mission Control, "The toilet shut down on its own, and I have a blinking amber fault light." The malfunction disabled the urine collection function aboard what is the first fully functional toilet ever installed on a deep-space mission.
ndtv
+2

Published
3 hours ago
ndtv
Artemis II Moon Mission First To Have Toilet On Board - NDTV
jcpost
🎥Artemis II astronauts reach orbit; troubleshoot issues with toilet system
nytimes
The Artemis II Toilet Had a Problem - The New York Times
+33 sources
space.com
A Fix Before Bedtime

NASA's associate administrator Amit Kshatriya described the problem as a "controller issue" during a post-launch news conference, estimating it would take several hours to troubleshoot. While engineers in Houston worked on a solution, at least one crew member resorted to a backup bag-and-funnel device known as a Collapsible Contingency Urinal. The toilet remained usable for solid waste throughout the episode.
businesstoday
+3

Koch, guided step-by-step by ground teams, disassembled portions of the system and restored the fan to working order. Capsule communicator Amy Dill then radioed the crew: "Happy to report that toilet is go for use. We do recommend letting the system get to operating speed before donating fluid, and then letting it run a little bit after donation."
ndtv
+2

6 sources
Communications Hiccup and Mission Status

The toilet was not the only wrinkle on launch night. About 51 minutes into the flight, during a planned handover between NASA's Tracking and Data Relay Satellites, ground teams temporarily lost the ability to hear the crew, though uplink communications remained intact. NASA Administrator Jared Isaacman said at a press conference that "there were no issues with the vehicle itself" and that contact was quickly restored.
mirror
+1
youtube

Neither issue threatened the mission's trajectory. The Orion spacecraft completed its apogee raise burn roughly two hours after liftoff, pushing the high point of its orbit to about 43,760 miles above Earth — higher than any astronauts have flown since Apollo 17 in 1972. The crew settled in for a four-hour nap before waking at 7 a.m. EDT on Thursday to prepare for the perigee raise burn, the next step toward translunar injection.
nasa
+2

6 sources
A Historic Mission Moves Forward

Artemis II lifted off at 6:35 p.m. EDT on Wednesday, April 1, from Kennedy Space Center's Launch Complex 39B, carrying Commander Reid Wiseman, Pilot Victor Glover, Koch, and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen on an approximately 10-day lunar flyby. The mission is designed to loop around the moon and return the crew to a Pacific Ocean splashdown, testing Orion's systems ahead of a planned lunar landing on a future Artemis flight.
nasa
+2

NASA's Artemis II crew orbits Earth after historic moonshot launch

NASA's four Artemis II astronauts have reached a stable orbit, clearing the first critical milestone of their journey to the Moon. The crew's Orion capsule successfully separated from the Space Launch System rocket and completed its initial orbital checks, with a trans-lunar injection burn planned for Thursday evening that will send them on their way to the lunar surface.

Published
10 hours ago
nasa
Artemis II Flight Update: Apogee Raise Burn Complete, Crew Looks Ahead to Proximity Operations
cbsnews
Artemis II crew begins "crazy first day" in space after exhilarating launch
foxnews
Artemis launch live: NASA Artemis II launch time, countdown and updates
+22 sources
nasa.gov
A "Crazy First Day" in Orbit

The Space Launch System rocket launched at 6:35 p.m. EDT on April 1, 2026, from Launch Complex 39B, producing nearly 9 million pounds of thrust as it carried Commander Reid Wiseman, Pilot Victor Glover, Mission Specialists Christina Koch and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen into space. The mission marks the first time a woman, a Black astronaut and a Canadian will travel to the Moon.
foxnews
+2

The crew spent their first 24 hours in a highly elliptical Earth orbit, putting Orion through exhaustive system checks. "It is a crazy first day," Wiseman told CBS News, describing the need to verify that the capsule can scrub carbon dioxide, provide drinking water and handle basic human functions before pressing on toward the Moon.
cbsnews

Not everything went smoothly. Koch reported a fault light while checking out the capsule's toilet system shortly after reaching orbit. Flight controllers told the crew the toilet could not spin up and advised using contingency bags for urine collection while engineers worked on a repair plan.
nasa
+1

4 sources
Proximity Operations and Next Steps

NASA confirmed that the apogee raise burn was successfully completed, fine-tuning Orion's orbit. A key early milestone came when Glover took manual control of the spacecraft and maneuvered it relative to the detached upper stage of the SLS rocket during a roughly 70-minute proximity operations demonstration. Glover described the thruster firing as producing "a little rumble, like driving on a rocky road".
cbsnews
+1

The crew was expected to take two four-hour rest periods early Thursday before NASA's mission management team reviews Orion's performance and clears the spacecraft for the trans-lunar injection burn. That six-minute engine firing, planned for Thursday evening, will increase the capsule's velocity by about 900 mph and send it on a free-return trajectory around the Moon.
cbsnews

2 sources
The Road to the Moon and Beyond

The approximately 10-day mission will carry the crew on a loop around the Moon without landing or entering lunar orbit. The astronauts are expected to pass within about 4,100 miles of the lunar surface and surpass the distance record set by Apollo 13 in 1970. Splashdown is targeted for April 10 in the Pacific Ocean off Southern California.
foxnews
+2

"This is a test flight," NASA Administrator Jared Isaacman told CBS News. "This is the opening act in a series of missions that will send astronauts to and from the moon with great frequency as we return to stay".
cbsnews

3 sources

"We're pretty fortunate as a crew to have a toilet with a door on this tiny spacecraft," he said. It is "the one place that we can go during the mission where we can actually feel like we're alone for a moment". NASA anticipated the possibility of a...
NASA's Artemis II set to launch Wednesday with unprecedented medical research
The mission's health research agenda extends beyond radiation. NASA's Human Research Program will collect data on fluid shifts, vestibular disruption, immune system changes, and crew behavioral health using wearable ARCHER sensors and saliva swabs measuring stress hormones. UCF's recently established Center for Aerospace and Extreme Environments Medicine is among the institutions working to...

Altman says he killed Sora to avoid addictive design

OpenAI CEO Sam Altman sat down for his first interview since the company abruptly shuttered its Sora video app, telling the Mostly Human podcast on Tuesday that he was unwilling to build the kind of addictive engagement features that would have made the product commercially viable. The wide-ranging conversation, conducted by veteran tech journalist Laurie Segall, also touched on OpenAI's Pentagon contracts, AI ethics, and raising children in an age of artificial intelligence.

A Billion-Dollar Deal Undone

OpenAI announced on March 24 that it would discontinue Sora, the short-form video generation tool it launched in late 2024. The move immediately killed a $1 billion deal with Walt Disney Co., announced in December, that would have given Sora users licensed access to more than 200 Disney, Marvel, Pixar, and Star Wars characters. Disney learned of the shutdown less than an hour before the public announcement, according to a Wall Street Journal investigation.

The jury awarded $6 million in combined compensatory and punitive damages, finding that both companies acted with "malice, oppression, or fraud" in creating features like infinite scroll and algorithmic content recommendations.

The company plans to redirect computing resources toward coding tools and enterprise customers, a shift that mirrors the strategy of rival Anthropic, whose Claude Code product had been gaining ground with software developers. Sora's research team will continue working on world simulation models aimed at advancing robotics, according to an OpenAI spokesperson. Artemis II crew eyes lunar trajectory burn after orbit test

Less than 24 hours after launching on the first crewed lunar mission in more than half a century, the four astronauts aboard NASA's Orion spacecraft successfully completed a manual proximity operations demonstration in high Earth orbit, guiding their capsule to within roughly 30 feet of a discarded rocket stage in a rehearsal for future docking missions at the Moon.

The roughly 70-minute exercise, carried out on the evening of April 1 shortly after the crew separated from the interim cryogenic propulsion stage (ICPS) that had boosted them into orbit, marked one of the earliest and most closely watched objectives of the Artemis II mission.
nasa
+1

Published
5 hours ago
nasa
Proximity Operations Complete, Perigee Raise Burn Up Next - NASA
nasa
Artemis II Flight Update: Apogee Raise Burn Complete, Crew Looks ...
nasa
Key Test Drive of Orion on NASA's Artemis II to Aid Future Missions
+33 sources
space.com
Flying by Hand

After Orion — which the crew named "Integrity" — separated from the spent ICPS upper stage, the spacecraft performed an automated backflip to face the stage. At about 300 feet away, Commander Reid Wiseman, Pilot Victor Glover, Mission Specialist Christina Koch, and Canadian Space Agency astronaut Jeremy Hansen took manual control, using translational and rotational hand controllers to inch the 25-ton capsule toward a two-foot target mounted on the ICPS. Using onboard cameras and the European Service Module's reaction control thrusters, the crew maneuvered Orion to within approximately 30 feet of the stage before backing away and repeating the approach from a second angle.
nasa
+2

"It's a good stand-in for what crews will see when they dock with Starship on Artemis III and to the Gateway on future missions," NASA engineer Howard Anderson said of the exercise in a pre-mission briefing. The demonstration concluded with an automated departure burn, after which the ICPS fired its own engine to re-enter the atmosphere over a remote stretch of the Pacific Ocean.
esa
+2

5 sources
What Comes Next

With proximity operations complete, the crew settled in for a brief rest period before being awakened at 7 a.m. EDT on Thursday, April 2, to prepare for a perigee raise burn designed to further shape Orion's orbit. The day's central event will be the translunar injection burn — an approximately six-minute firing of the European Service Module's main engine that, if all systems check out, will send the crew on an irreversible four-day trajectory toward the Moon.
nasa
+3

Flight controllers are expected to convene a go/no-go meeting before committing to the burn. If it proceeds, the Artemis II crew will become the first humans to leave low Earth orbit since the Apollo 17 astronauts did so in December 1972.
nbcnews
+2

5 sources

MediaTek, Qualcomm cut 4nm chip output as memory costs soar

MediaTek and Qualcomm are pulling back sharply on production of 4nm mobile processors, cutting wafer starts by roughly 15% year-over-year — a reduction equivalent to 15 to 20 million chip units — as soaring memory prices squeeze the smartphone supply chain, according to a report from TrendForce published this week. The cuts target chips used primarily in mid-range and budget smartphones, a segment now bearing the brunt of what industry observers are calling demand destruction.
linkedin
+1

Published
5 hours ago
wccftech
MediaTek, Qualcomm Reportedly Slash Shipments Of 4nm Mobile ...
evertiq
Memory price surge threatens global smartphone production in 2026
reuters
Smartphone market set for biggest-ever decline in 2026 on memory ...
cnet
Smartphone Sales to Plummet 13% in 2026 Due to RAM Crisis ...
asiafinancial.com
Memory Crisis Reshapes the Supply Chain

The production pullback stems from a cascading crisis that began in the memory market. Surging demand for high-bandwidth memory from AI data center operators — including Meta, Google, and Microsoft — has consumed much of the global DRAM supply, sending contract prices for mainstream smartphone memory modules up nearly 200% in the first quarter of 2026 compared to the same period last year, according to TrendForce. Memory, which historically made up 10 to 15% of a smartphone's bill of materials, now accounts for 30 to 40%.
evertiq

The result has been a wave of price increases across the industry. Samsung has raised prices on multiple tablet and smartphone models, and Chinese OEMs reliant on budget-friendly devices have been especially hard hit. With consumer demand softening, MediaTek and Qualcomm have opted to scale back 4nm wafer orders — estimated at 20,000 to 30,000 fewer wafers — to avoid building up excess inventory.
wccftech

2 sources
Broader Market in Retreat

The chip production cuts are the latest symptom of what the International Data Corporation has called the smartphone industry's most severe downturn in over a decade. IDC projected in late February that global smartphone shipments would fall 12.9% in 2026 to roughly 1.12 billion units, a sharp revision from earlier estimates of a decline between 0.9% and 5.2%. The downturn is expected to hit low-cost Android manufacturers hardest, while Apple and Samsung may gain market share as smaller rivals struggle.
reuters
+1

Counterpoint Research had earlier forecast an overall 7% decline in smartphone SoC shipments for 2026, with MediaTek facing an estimated 8-percentage-point drop — the steepest among major vendors — owing to its heavy exposure to entry-level chipsets. Qualcomm's shipments were projected to fall about 2 percentage points.
sammobile

3 sources
What Comes Next

The Iran conflict has added further strain, with the closure of the Strait of Hormuz disrupting helium supplies critical to semiconductor manufacturing. Meanwhile, the decline in spot DDR5 prices has offered little relief so far, as analysts say contract pricing — the metric that drives OEM purchasing decisions — remains elevated. For MediaTek and Qualcomm, the near-term outlook hinges on whether memory costs stabilize before deeper cuts become necessary.
wccftech

1 source

Researchers discover protein that blocks nerve repair after spinal injury

Researchers at the Icahn School of Medicine at Mount Sinai have identified a protein that acts as a molecular "brake" on nerve repair, a discovery that could eventually lead to new treatments for spinal cord and peripheral nerve injuries. The findings, published March 31 in the journal Nature, show that disabling the aryl hydrocarbon receptor (AHR) in neurons shifts them from a stress-management mode into one that favors regrowth of damaged axons.
nature
+1

Published
5 hours ago
mountsinai
Researchers Identify Molecular “Brake” That Limits Axonal ...
beckersspine
Mount Sinai study finds 'molecular brake' limiting spine, nerve repair
nature
AhR inhibition promotes axon regeneration via a stress–growth switch
pmc.ncbi.nlm.nih
Aryl hydrocarbon receptor restricts axon regeneration of DRG ... - PMC
Bhautik Patel
·
unsplash.com
A Cellular Tug of War

When neurons are injured, they face a trade-off: protect themselves from immediate damage or begin rebuilding severed connections. The Mount Sinai team found that AHR, a transcription factor originally known for sensing environmental toxins, plays a central role in tipping that balance toward self-preservation.
mountsinai
+1

"We discovered that AHR functions like a brake that shifts neurons toward managing stress rather than rebuilding damaged connections," said Hongyan Zou, a professor of neurosurgery and neuroscience at Mount Sinai and the study's senior author.
mountsinai

When AHR signaling is active after injury, it reinforces protein quality control — a process called proteostasis — helping neurons cope with stress but simultaneously suppressing the production of new proteins needed for growth. By genetically deleting AHR from neurons or blocking it with drugs, the researchers reversed this pattern. Neurons began producing more proteins and activated growth-related pathways, leading to improved axon regrowth in mouse models of both peripheral nerve injury and spinal cord injury.
nature
+2

The team also found that the regenerative response depends on a partner molecule called HIF-1α, which helps regulate genes involved in metabolism and tissue repair.
nature
+1

3 sources
A Path Toward Treatment

The discovery carries particular therapeutic promise because several drugs that inhibit AHR are already being tested in clinical trials for other conditions, such as cancer. That existing pipeline could accelerate the path toward studying these compounds in neurological injuries.
beckersspine
+1

"By releasing this brake, we can push neurons into a state that favors repair," Zou said.
mountsinai

The study remains at an early, preclinical stage — all experiments were conducted in mice — and translating the results to human patients will require further research. Still, the work offers a new molecular target in a field where treatment options for spinal cord injury remain limited, and where the underlying biology of why adult neurons fail to regenerate has long frustrated scientists.

UQ researchers map how neuroblastoma tumors evade the immune system

Researchers at the University of Queensland have created an unprecedented spatial map of neuroblastoma — one of the deadliest childhood cancers — revealing that the tumors deploy molecular "shields" and co-opt immune cells as "bodyguards" to survive, according to a study published in Genome Medicine on April 1, 2026.
eurekalert

The findings identify a specific protein, GPX4, as a key vulnerability in high-risk neuroblastoma, with drugs already in clinical trials for adult cancers that could potentially be repurposed to treat children.

Published
Apr 1, 2026
eurekalert
scientists uncover the hidden defences of a deadly childhood cancer
scienmag
Unveiling the Hidden Defenses: How Scientists Are Battling a Deadly
chop
Children's Hospital of Philadelphia researchers find promising ...
linkedin
2026 Immunotherapy Grant Now Open for Researchers - LinkedIn
frontiersin.org
A Satellite View of Cancer

Neuroblastoma typically strikes children under age five and accounts for roughly 10 percent of all pediatric cancer deaths. Despite decades of aggressive treatment, survival rates for the most dangerous cases have remained stubbornly low.
eurekalert

Associate Professor Fernando Guimaraes of UQ's Frazer Institute led the team that used spatial multi-omics technology to map tumor samples from 27 pediatric patients, constructing high-resolution two-dimensional maps showing exactly where cancer cells, immune cells, stromal tissue, and blood vessels sit in relation to one another.
scienmag
+1

"Before this technology, it was a bit like trying to understand a city just by reading a list of its residents; you'd have no idea who lives next to whom or which neighbourhoods are dangerous," Guimaraes said. "Our study is one of the first in the world to use it on this type of childhood cancer."
eurekalert

2 sources
The Shield and the Bodyguards

The mapping revealed that high-risk neuroblastoma tumors carry a hidden defense against ferroptosis, a natural cancer-killing process triggered by the buildup of toxic lipid peroxides inside cells. The protein GPX4 acts as a shield, neutralizing those peroxides and allowing cancer cells to survive. Certain immune cells that would normally attack the tumor were found instead to act as protectors, fostering an environment that supports tumor growth.
scienmag
+1

When researchers switched off GPX4 in laboratory models, neuroblastoma cells died — confirming it as a promising drug target.
eurekalert

2 sources
From Lab to Bedside

Study first author Dr. Cui Tu said drugs designed to strip away the GPX4 shield are already being tested in adults. "Our findings suggest these drugs could be repurposed to treat children with high-risk neuroblastoma, potentially reaching clinical trials in coming years," she said. "This is the kind of discovery that can move from the lab to a child's bedside relatively quickly because the drug pathway already exists."
eurekalert

Associate Professor Wayne Nicholls, Clinical Director of the Ian Frazer Centre for Children's Immunotherapy Research and Director of Oncology Services at Queensland Children's Hospital, called the work a source of genuine hope. "This research uncovers a genuine vulnerability in the most aggressive tumours, one that could be targeted with new treatments," Nicholls said. "For our patients and their families, that is a real reason for hope."
eurekalert

Study links Down syndrome brain changes to overactive RNA editing enzyme

Scientists have identified a molecular mechanism that may explain how the brain develops differently in people with Down syndrome, tracing the disruption to an overactive RNA editing enzyme driven by the extra copy of chromosome 21.

The findings, published Tuesday in Nature Communications, come from a collaborative study co-led by researchers at the Icahn School of Medicine at Mount Sinai and the Lieber Institute for Brain Development. The research shows that trisomy 21 causes overexpression of the gene ADARB1 — which encodes an enzyme also known as ADAR2 — leading to premature and excessive editing of RNA in developing fetal brain cells.
nature
+1

Published
Mar 31, 2026
nature
Trisomy 21 Drives ADARB1 Overexpression and Premature RNA ...
mountsinai
Scientists Identify Dysregulation of RNA Editing as ... - Mount Sinai
news-medical
Excessive RNA editing enzyme alters brain circuit formation in Down ...
bioengineer
Researchers Link RNA Editing Dysregulation to Abnormal Fetal Brain
news.virginia.edu
How Extra Chromosome 21 Reshapes the Brain

The research team examined brain tissue samples collected at mid-gestation from 20 fetuses with trisomy 21 and 27 unaffected controls, using advanced RNA sequencing to map gene activity and RNA editing across the transcriptome. They found widespread disruption of gene expression, with ADARB1 emerging as one of the most consistently overexpressed genes.
bioengineer
+1

The excess ADARB1 enzyme was associated with heightened RNA editing — a natural post-transcriptional process that modifies RNA sequences to fine-tune protein function in neurons. In typical development, this editing increases gradually during fetal brain growth. In trisomy 21, the process occurs earlier and more intensely.
mountsinai

The team observed excessive editing in genes including GRIA2, GRIA3, GRIK2, and GABRA3 — glutamate and GABA-receptor genes that regulate how neurons send and receive signals. These premature molecular changes are predicted to alter the balance between excitatory and inhibitory signaling during critical periods when neural circuits are being established.
nature
+1

"We found that RNA editing occurs earlier and more extensively in trisomy 21 and this early shift may influence how brain circuits are formed from the very beginning," said Michael S. Breen, Associate Professor of Genetics and Genomic Sciences at Mount Sinai.
news-medical
+1

4 sources
Robust Findings Across Multiple Datasets

To validate the results, the researchers performed a combined analysis of nine independent human trisomy 21 datasets, which consistently showed the same pattern of elevated ADARB1 levels and increased RNA editing. The reproducibility across diverse cell types — from stem cells and neural progenitor cells to fibroblasts and postmortem brain tissue — underscored the biological robustness of the findings.
news-medical
+2

"These findings redefine Down syndrome neuropathology to include disrupted post-transcription regulation and establish RNA editing as a measurable biomarker of early brain circuit development and a promising avenue for therapeutic intervention," said Joseph D. Buxbaum, Professor of Psychiatry, Neuroscience, and Genetics and Genomic Sciences at Mount Sinai.
mountsinai

UCL team grows human myelin in the lab for the first time

Researchers at University College London have built a laboratory model of nerve fibres that more closely mimics the softness and structure of real brain tissue — and in doing so, may have uncovered a key reason why promising multiple sclerosis drugs repeatedly fail in human trials.

Published
Mar 31, 2026
ucl
Model of brain wiring could shorten path to new medicines
nature
Tunable hydrogel-based micropillar arrays for myelination studies
medicalxpress
Brain wiring model could shorten path to new medicines
miragenews
Brain Wiring Model May Speed New Drug Discovery | Mirage News
news.ohsu.edu
A Closer Match to the Human Brain

The model, published on March 29 in Nature Methods, uses tiny hydrogel pillars tens of times thinner than a human hair to replicate axons, the long nerve fibres that carry electrical signals through the brain and spinal cord. Unlike earlier models made from rigid plastics, the hydrogel pillars can be tuned to match the softness of real axons — a property the researchers say is critical for evaluating potential drugs.
nature
+1

When the team grew myelin-producing brain cells called oligodendrocytes around these pillars, they found that candidate drugs designed to promote myelin repair performed markedly worse on the softer, more life-like pillars than on their rigid predecessors. The finding suggests that commonly used hard models, which can be hundreds of times stiffer than actual axons, may generate misleading results during early drug screening.
ucl

"Our work suggests that commonly used rigid models, hundreds of times stiffer than real axons, can generate misleading drug hits," said senior author Professor Emad Moeendarbary of UCL Mechanical Engineering. "We believe that our more life-like model can be used as a more robust early test of drug candidates and as a platform to discover new drugs."
ucl

2 sources
First Human-Cell Myelin Grown in the Lab

The study also marks the first time myelin has been successfully grown from human cells in a laboratory setting, according to UCL. Previous work had demonstrated myelination using animal-derived cells or 3D brain organoids, but the UCL team achieved multilayered myelin wrapping around individual axon-like structures using human oligodendrocytes.
medicalxpress
+2

The micropillars were fabricated using photolithography to create tiny moulds, which were then filled with hydrogel. The five-year effort was led primarily by PhD student Soufian Lasli and Dr Claire Vinel.
ucl

3 sources
Implications for MS and Beyond

In multiple sclerosis, the immune system attacks myelin, disrupting the signals that control movement, thought, and sensation. The brain's ability to repair this damage declines with age and repeated attacks. The same process of myelin deterioration plays a role in Alzheimer's, Parkinson's, and motor neurone disease.
ucl

Professor Moeendarbary said the team hopes the platform will enable "more reliable validation of potential drugs before they reach patients in clinical trials". The research involved collaborators from UCL, Universidad de Malaga, and the University of Nottingham.
ucl

1 source

The discovery carries particular therapeutic promise because several drugs that inhibit AHR are already being tested in clinical trials for other conditions, such as cancer. That existing pipeline could accelerate the path toward studying these compounds in neurological injuries. "By releasing this brake, we can push neurons into a state that favors repair," Zou said. Because the nanoparticles do not integrate genetic material into the host genome, the therapeutic effects are temporary — mRNA lasts several days and plasmid DNA several months. DRAM and NAND prices set for another record quarter as electronics costs surge

A convergence of AI-driven memory demand, geopolitical conflict, and tightening raw material controls is driving the steepest price increases in consumer electronics in more than a decade. From gaming consoles to laptops to smartphones, the costs of PCs and electronics are climbing sharply — with no relief expected before late 2027.

Memory Prices Shatter Records

TrendForce, the semiconductor market research firm, reported this week that conventional DRAM contract prices are forecast to rise 58% to 63% quarter-over-quarter in Q2 2026, while NAND Flash prices are expected to jump 70% to 75% — following Q1 increases that already saw DRAM contracts climb by a record 90% to 95%. The root cause remains the same: memory manufacturers like Samsung, SK Hynix, and Micron are redirecting production capacity toward high-margin AI server chips, leaving consumer electronics starved for supply.

+2
