A Widening War

The conflict traces back to February 28, when the United States and Israel launched a joint military operation against Iran, killing Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei. Hezbollah responded on March 2 by firing rockets toward Israel for the first time since a ceasefire took effect in November 2024, triggering a massive Israeli aerial campaign across Lebanon. Israel launched a ground invasion on March 16, pushing armored and infantry divisions into southern Lebanon.

Lebanon's defense minister condemned the statement as an effort to impose a "new occupation" of Lebanese territory.

Fortnite to sell AI 'brainrot' meme skins Friday

Epic Games is bringing viral AI-generated meme characters into Fortnite as purchasable cosmetics, with the Tung Tung Tung Sahur and Ballerina Cappuccina skins set to arrive in the item shop on Friday, April 3, 2026, at 8 PM ET. The move marks the battle royale's first official collaboration with so-called "Italian brainrot" content — AI-generated characters that became internet sensations in 2025 — and has already drawn sharp criticism from players and artists alike.

beebom.com
From AI Meme to Fortnite Skin

Tung Tung Tung Sahur, often called "Triple T," originated as part of a wave of AI-generated brainrot memes in early 2025. The character is an anthropomorphic wooden plank wielding a baseball bat, paired with an Indonesian voice-over referencing the Ramadan tradition of drumming to wake people for the pre-dawn Sahur meal. The meme belongs to a broader genre of AI-created characters narrated by an Italian text-to-speech voice, which also spawned viral figures like Bombardiro Crocodilo and Tralalero Tralala.
knowyourmeme

The skins were first teased in the Fortnite Chapter 7 Season 2 trailer and formally confirmed after dataminers decrypted files from the April 1 update. According to dataminer ShiinaBR, as reported by VICE, the full Brainrot bundle will include both character skins, themed pickaxes, and weapon wraps, with the bundle expected to cost around 3,300 V-Bucks and individual skins priced at roughly 1,500 V-Bucks.
beebom
+2

4 sources
Player Backlash Over AI Content

The announcement has intensified an ongoing debate within Fortnite's community over the use of AI-generated material. A Reddit post calling for the ability to hide certain skins from view garnered over 4,000 upvotes, with one user arguing that a toggle option — similar to the existing feature for blocking toxic emotes — would let players "save our eyes from seeing brain rot". Others have proposed a more direct form of protest: targeting anyone wearing the skins in-game, echoing the community response to the Tesla Cybertruck cosmetic.
thegamer

The Gamer noted that Epic Games CEO Tim Sweeney has been a vocal AI advocate, and the brainrot skins follow previous AI-adjacent additions to the game, including an AI companion Darth Vader feature that was quickly manipulated by players. Gfinity Esports described the collaboration as "a step too far," highlighting concerns about artistic integrity and the promotion of AI-generated content to Fortnite's predominantly young audience.
gfinityesports
+1

2 sources
A Broader Industry Tension

The controversy arrives amid wider gaming industry friction over AI art. Fortnite itself faced accusations in late 2025 that Chapter 7 Season 1 included AI-generated in-game posters, prompting an artist at Epic to publicly defend their work. The brainrot skins represent a different dynamic — rather than denying AI involvement, Epic is openly embracing AI-born characters as a commercial product, a distinction that has only sharpened the backlash.

LinearGame demos 'engine-less' AI game platform at GDC

LinearGame, an AI-native gaming startup with teams in Singapore and the United States, presented its Yoroll platform at this year's Game Developers Conference and NVIDIA GTC, demonstrating what the company describes as a way to turn AI-generated video into structured, playable gaming experiences.
businesswire
+1

The announcement, made via a Business Wire press release on Tuesday, marks one of the more concrete efforts to move AI-generated video games beyond research demos and toward viable products. According to the release, what set LinearGame's demonstrations apart from typical AI game previews was the focus on playable implementations rather than standalone model outputs or research benchmarks.
venturebeat
+1

Published
23 hours ago
morningstar
The World Model Revolution: How Yoroll.ai is Building the First ...
news.marketersmedia
Funding Round Backs LinearGame's Vision for AI-Driven Playable ...
businesswire
The World Model Revolution: How Yoroll.ai is Building the First ...
twstalker
Yoroll @YorollAI - Twitter Profile - TwStalker
youtube.com
How the Platform Works

Yoroll operates on a three-layer architecture that the company first detailed in February. The "Expression Layer" uses world models — including Google's Genie 3 and LinearGame's proprietary Roll-01 — to generate visual output and handle physical feedback such as character movement. A "Judgment Layer" employs a Vision-Language Model that acts as a real-time referee, monitoring the video stream to identify game events like dodging attacks or collecting items. The "State Layer" stores underlying data such as inventory, health points, and branching plot points in a traditional database, ensuring player progress remains intact even if the AI produces visual inconsistencies.
morningstar
+1

The result is what LinearGame calls an "engine-less" game — one that uses generative video as its primary rendering layer instead of simulating 3D environments through conventional game engines.
businesswire

2 sources
From Concept to Creator Tool

Beyond its studio titles, the Yoroll platform is designed as a creator tool. The company says it allows storytellers to transform text prompts, photos, and short clips into branching narratives with gameplay components including multiple choices, quick-time events, and light combat — all without code or 3D tools. LinearGame opened a creator beta for the platform, which it describes as enabling "video-native interaction designed for storytellers and game makers — turning passive generative video into playable, branching narratives".
news.marketersmedia
+3

4 sources
Broader Context

The presentation arrives amid growing interest in AI-driven game development. At GDC 2026, Google Cloud showcased AI tools aimed at creating what it called "living games," while NVIDIA demonstrated local real-time AI video generation. Unity also reported stronger-than-expected quarterly results driven partly by its AI-related offerings. LinearGame, which closed a multi-million-dollar pre-seed round led by HT Opportunity Fund in late 2025, plans to use the funding to expand its engineering team and launch titles across PC, console, mobile, and web.
aiandgames
youtube
bonega

Activist ship rams krill trawler off Antarctica

A vessel operated by the Captain Paul Watson Foundation collided with a Norwegian-owned industrial krill trawler in Antarctic waters on Tuesday, escalating a confrontation over krill fishing in one of the planet's most ecologically sensitive regions.

Published
18 hours ago
cbsnews
Activist ship's collision with krill trawler off Antarctica called ...
reuters
Activist vessel collides with krill harvesting vessel off ...
facebook
The Captain Paul Watson Foundation Disrupts Aker Krill ... - Facebook
apnews
Activist vessel collides with krill trawler in Antarctic confrontation
yahoo.com
The Collision

The M/V Bandero, a 65-meter vessel operated by the foundation, struck the port side of the Norwegian-flagged Antarctic Sea, owned by Aker BioMarine, during what the activist group described as a five-hour "direct intervention" against krill fishing operations. A two-minute video provided to The Associated Press by Aker QRILL Co. shows the Bandero slowly approaching the stern of the fishing vessel and making contact at a slight angle.
apnews
+2

Aker said Wednesday that the Bandero came within centimeters of striking a diesel tank on the Antarctic Sea, which it said could have caused an environmental disaster in waters teeming with whale species, seals, and seabirds that depend on the Southern Ocean's krill population. The company described the collision as a "deliberate attack" and said it would pursue all available legal action. Its multinational crew was shaken but unharmed.
cbsnews
+1

3 sources
Dueling Accounts

The two sides offered sharply different characterizations of the incident. In a statement to Reuters, the Captain Paul Watson Foundation called it "an accidental collision" and said it was committed to "lawful, responsible, non-violent action in defense of marine ecosystems". In its own press release, however, the foundation described its tactics as "aggressive nonviolence" and said its crew, led by French activist Lamya Essemlali, had deployed metal net-shredding devices and disrupted all krill fishing by two Aker-owned vessels over more than five hours.
reuters
+2

The foundation also shared images showing crew members launching the net-disrupting equipment into the water.
cbsnews

3 sources
Operation Krill Wars

The confrontation is part of the foundation's "Operation Krill Wars" campaign, launched in February when the Bandero departed Australia for the Southern Ocean. The campaign targets what the group calls the destructive scale of industrial krill harvesting in Antarctic whale feeding grounds. Aker QRILL Co. is currently the largest harvester of Antarctic krill, accounting for more than 60 percent of the total catch quota, according to the foundation. Last season, factory trawlers harvested more than 620,000 tonnes of Antarctic krill, with over 70 percent taken directly from whale feeding grounds, the foundation said, adding that fishing nations are pushing to nearly double allowable catches to 1.2 million tonnes.
facebook
+1

Paul Watson, the veteran anti-whaling campaigner who founded the group, has warned that unchecked krill fishing threatens the entire Antarctic food web. "If the ocean dies, we die," Watson has said. "Krill are the blood of the sea".
paulwatsonfoundation

3 sources

NATO chief Rutte to visit Washington as Trump threatens alliance exit

NATO Secretary-General Mark Rutte is set to travel to Washington, D.C., next week for meetings with U.S. officials, a NATO spokesperson confirmed on Tuesday, describing the trip as "long-planned." The visit, first reported by The Wall Street Journal, comes at one of the most fraught moments in the alliance's history, as President Donald Trump publicly entertains the possibility of withdrawing the United States from NATO over European allies' refusal to back the war in Iran.

Trump Threatens NATO Exit

No details about the agenda of Rutte's visit were immediately available, but the backdrop could hardly be more charged. In an interview with Britain's Telegraph published Wednesday, Trump said his reconsideration of U.S. membership in NATO goes "beyond reconsideration," calling the 77-year-old defense bloc a "paper tiger". He doubled down in a separate interview with Reuters, saying he is "absolutely" considering an attempt to exit the alliance.
time
+2

Trump has been particularly frustrated by the refusal of European allies to assist in reopening the Strait of Hormuz, which Iran has effectively blockaded since the U.S.-Israeli military campaign began on February 28. According to The Wall Street Journal, Trump has discussed the idea of withdrawing from NATO with advisers, including Secretary of State Marco Rubio, if allied nations do not help reopen the waterway. White House spokesperson Anna Kelly said Trump "has expressed his dissatisfaction with NATO and other allies," adding that "the United States will remember".

+1

5 sources
Legal and Political Barriers

Any attempt by Trump to pull the United States out of NATO would face a legal obstacle. A 2023 law, spearheaded in part by Rubio himself when he served in the Senate, bars the president from withdrawing without congressional approval. Whether that provision would deter Trump remains an open question, as CBS News noted his comments may also serve as leverage over allies to increase defense contributions.
cbsnews
+1

2 sources
Rutte's Balancing Act

Rutte, a former Dutch prime minister who took over as NATO secretary-general in 2024, has cultivated a reputation as a "Trump whisperer" able to navigate the U.S. president's transactional approach to alliances. He has made multiple trips to Washington during the Trump presidency, including visits that produced a framework agreement on Greenland and Arctic security in January and talks on defense spending last spring.
thetimes
+4

The upcoming visit takes place as Trump has told reporters he expects U.S. forces to leave Iran in "two to three weeks" and is scheduled to address the nation Wednesday evening to provide an update on the conflict. Rubio told Fox News on Tuesday that the U.S. may need to "re-examine" its relationship with NATO once the war ends.

Overwatch launches 'Underwatch' April Fools' mode amid fake sequel rumors

Claims of an "Overwatch 3" announcement featuring a full PvE campaign spread online on April 1, but no such reveal took place. Blizzard Entertainment did not announce a sequel at any event on that date. Instead, the company launched its annual April Fools' Day celebration: a limited-time arcade mode called "Underwatch," running from April 1 through April 13.

An April Fools' Prank, Not a Sequel

The Underwatch event features absurd hero kit changes, googly eyes on every character, and physics that, as the developers put it, "will follow no rules". Among the sillier adjustments, Roadhog's hook no longer pulls enemies but instead "slows, hacks, anti-heals, burns, and reveals" them, while the hero Mizuki gained a stack of three hats. Mei was temporarily reclassified as a tank, and Cassidy can fire bullets by pointing his index finger.
blizzard
+2

The fake Overwatch 3 rumor likely gained traction because of the date and longstanding community frustration over the absence of PvE content. Blizzard originally promised a full cooperative story campaign as a centerpiece of Overwatch 2 when it was announced at BlizzCon 2019, but cancelled that ambitious PvE mode in May 2023. A smaller set of paid story missions released later that year sold poorly, and by early 2024, former developers told outlets that even those limited PvE efforts had been deprioritized.
outof
+2

6 sources
Overwatch's Actual 2026 Direction

Rather than pursuing a sequel, Blizzard has taken the opposite approach. In February 2026, the company dropped the "2" from the game's title, rebranding it simply as Overwatch. Game director Aaron Keller's team explicitly said the change was made so players would not worry about an "Overwatch 3". The rebrand accompanied a major content push: a year-long narrative arc called "The Reign of Talon," ten new heroes across six seasons, and a new competitive structure. A separate mobile spin-off, Overwatch Rush, was also announced in February as a top-down hero shooter in early development.
overwatch.fandom
+3

Community calls for PvE have not subsided, with forum posts and speculation continuing into 2026. But for now, Blizzard's focus remains on live PvP content and seasonal storytelling rather than a standalone cooperative campaign — and any April 1 claims to the contrary were, fittingly, a joke.

Share
Trump downplays Iran's uranium stockpile as arms race fears mount

More than a month into the U.S.-Israeli war on Iran, the conflict's failure to neutralize Tehran's nuclear materials has raised alarm among arms control experts that the Middle East could be headed toward a new era of nuclear proliferation, with regional powers reassessing their own need for atomic weapons.

Despite President Donald Trump's repeated assertions that a core objective of Operation Epic Fury is to ensure Iran "never possesses a nuclear weapon," Iran retains roughly 441 kilograms of uranium enriched to 60 percent purity — a short technical step from the 90 percent weapons-grade threshold. According to Fortune, citing diplomatic officials, the stockpile is sufficient for roughly a dozen nuclear warheads if further refined, with U.S. officials estimating specifically 11 bombs. In a CBS News interview aired this week, Trump appeared to downplay the stockpile, saying, "I don't even think about it. I just know that it's so deeply buried it's going to be very hard for anybody" to reach it.
ynetnews
+4

Published
chathamhouse
The Iran war risks triggering a new wave of nuclear proliferation
dw
Will Iran war start a nuclear arms race in Middle East? - DW
wikipedia
2026 Iran war - Wikipedia
britannica
2026 Iran war | Explained, United States, Israel, Strait of ... - Britannica
nbcnews.com
A Dangerous Precedent

The war, launched on February 28 with joint U.S.-Israeli airstrikes that killed Supreme Leader Ali Khamenei and dozens of other officials, has paradoxically strengthened the case for nuclear weapons among states watching from the sidelines. As Georgia Cole, a research associate at Chatham House, wrote in an analysis published March 30, many states will absorb "a straightforward message: nuclear weapons deter attack in a way that conventional capabilities cannot".
wikipedia
+2

Prominent voices within Iran's regime are now arguing Tehran should withdraw from the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty and develop the bomb, according to Reuters. Iran's new supreme leader, Mojtaba Khamenei, is reported to be more hardline than his father on nuclear matters. This week, Iranian politicians publicly raised the prospect of an NPT exit.
chathamhouse
+2

5 sources
Regional Dominos

The ripple effects extend well beyond Iran. Saudi Arabia's Crown Prince Mohammed bin Salman has previously warned that the kingdom would pursue nuclear weapons if Iran does. Riyadh reportedly secured a nuclear cooperation agreement with Washington last year that would allow uranium enrichment — a deal that former IAEA director Robert Kelley told Bloomberg "bucks all precedent," calling it hypocritical given that the U.S. is "bombing Iran for" the very activities it would permit Saudi Arabia to pursue.
chathamhouse
+1

Kelsey Davenport, director for non-proliferation policy at the Arms Control Association, told DW that "there are a number of factors that will push states in the Gulf closer to nuclear weapons," though she cautioned that "significant technical and political hurdles" remain. Egypt is building a Russian-designed reactor on the Mediterranean coast, and Turkey is developing nuclear energy programs with Russia and potentially China.
dw

2 sources
Eroding Guardrails

The crisis unfolds against a backdrop of crumbling global arms control. The New START treaty between the U.S. and Russia expired in February with no replacement, China is expanding its nuclear arsenal, and Trump instructed the Pentagon to restart nuclear testing for the first time in 30 years. The upcoming NPT Review Conference in April and May will test whether the non-proliferation regime can hold, even as the war that was supposed to prevent a nuclear Iran may instead be accelerating the very outcome it sought to avoid.
chathamhouse

1 source

Pop Mart selloff deepens as short sellers pile on

Pop Mart has lost more than 30 percent of its value in just five trading sessions through March 31, extending a decline from its August all-time high to nearly 60 percent and erasing roughly $33 billion in market capitalization, according to Bloomberg. The selloff, which began after the Beijing-based toymaker reported 2025 earnings on March 25, has drawn a surge of bearish bets even as the company responds with its largest-ever share buyback program.

Earnings Spark a Rout

Pop Mart's full-year results were by most measures impressive: revenue nearly tripled to 37.12 billion yuan ($5.4 billion), while net profit surged 308 percent to 12.78 billion yuan. But the numbers failed to meet buyside expectations, and management's 2026 growth guidance of "no less than 20 percent" fell well short of the 30 percent the market had priced in.

+4

Wall Street Turns Bearish

The results triggered a wave of downgrades. Bank of America downgraded the stock from buy to neutral, slashing its target from HK$300 to HK$170, while China Merchants Securities International also moved to sell with a target of HK$127. HSBC, Goldman Sachs, UBS, Citi, Nomura, and Morgan Stanley all lowered their price targets.

Options traders pushed put contract volumes on Pop Mart to a record high on April 1. The stock's forward price-to-earnings ratio has collapsed to a record low of 10.3 times, less than half its three-year average of 24 times.

Buybacks Fail to Stem the Tide

Algorand surges after Google quantum paper highlights its defenses

Algorand saw its native token ALGO rally more than 20% on Monday and Tuesday after Google Quantum AI published a whitepaper that singled out the blockchain as a leading example of post-quantum cryptography deployed in the real world. The token climbed to an eight-week high near $0.105, crossing the $0.10 threshold for the first time since February, with trading volume surging nearly fivefold.
ambcrypto

The whitepaper, released March 30–31, warned that breaking the elliptic curve cryptography underpinning Bitcoin and most other blockchains could require fewer than 500,000 physical qubits — roughly 20 times fewer than Google's own 2019 estimate. Researchers from Google's quantum computing division, the University of California, Berkeley, and the Ethereum Foundation co-authored the paper, which framed 2029 as a practical migration deadline for the crypto industry.
thequantuminsider
+2

Why Algorand Stood Out

Among the blockchains examined, Algorand received particular attention. The paper described it as providing "an example of real-world deployment of PQC on an otherwise quantum-vulnerable blockchain," citing its live use of Falcon digital signatures for smart contracts and state proofs. Algorand was mentioned more than 30 times in the document, trailing only Bitcoin and Ethereum in the number of references, according to crypto.news. Other projects noted for early quantum-resistance efforts included QRL, Solana, and XRP Ledger, though none matched Algorand's depth of coverage in the report.

+3

ALGO's market capitalization approached $1 billion during the rally, and futures open interest jumped 55% to roughly $58.9 million, according to CoinGlass data cited by crypto.news. The move broke ALGO out of a descending channel that had capped gains since the start of the year, pushing the token above its 20-day, 50-day, and 100-day simple moving averages in rapid succession.
crypto

Analysts urged caution despite the euphoria. AMBCrypto noted that a cluster of short liquidations above $0.10 had already been swept and that Bitcoin's broader bearish bias could weigh on altcoins. ALGO holders were advised to watch whether the token can hold above $0.095 and reclaim $0.11 — a resistance level from early February — to confirm a sustained trend reversal rather than a one-day spike.

The surge also coincided with Algorand's recent integration into Swiss retail bank PostFinance, which gave its 2.5 million customers the ability to trade and hold ALGO directly. Still, the token remains far below its all-time high above $3, a reminder of how far the project has fallen from its early peaks even as its quantum-resistance credentials gain fresh relevance.

Iran war ripples through beauty, housing and pharma supply chains

The war in Iran and the resulting blockade of the Strait of Hormuz, now approaching its fifth week, is sending cost shocks through industries far removed from the battlefield — from Italian cosmetics firms to Indian luxury housing developers and Thailand's pharmaceutical regulators.

Published
16 hours ago
fashionnetwork
Cosmoprof 2026 welcomes 255,000 visitors from over 150 countries
english.aawsat

How the Iran-Israel conflict is driving up homebuilding costs in ...
hindustantimes
Will Strait of Hormuz disruption push up luxury apartment prices in ...
cnbc.com
Beauty Industry Feels the Squeeze

At Cosmoprof Worldwide Bologna, one of the cosmetics sector's largest trade fairs, which drew 255,000 visitors and 3,100 exhibitors from 68 countries last week, rising costs dominated the conversation among executives. Five industry leaders told Reuters that higher raw material and transport costs tied to surging oil prices and disrupted shipping were their chief concern.
fashionnetwork
+1

"We are beginning to see cost increases driven by energy price inflation, compounded by delivery delays," said Simone Dominici, CEO of Italian cosmetics group Kiko, who estimated additional logistics-related costs of about 1.5 million euros for the group over the year. Kiko operates more than 1,000 stores worldwide. Roberto Bottino, CEO of contract manufacturer Ancorotti Group, said lead times had stretched from eight weeks to 12 or 14 weeks as routes lengthened and ports grew congested, with some clients turning to rail transport to reach Asia.
english.aawsat

Yonwoo, a container maker for L'Oréal and K-beauty brands, said it was scrambling to secure plastic resin stocks needed to manufacture cosmetics pots. Italy produced 18 billion euros of cosmetics in 2025, including 8.4 billion euros in exports, making it the world's fifth-largest exporter of beauty products.
english.aawsat

2 sources
India's Luxury Housing Under Pressure

In India, the blockade is hitting construction costs hard. According to ANAROCK Group, steel prices have surged nearly 20 percent to around ₹72,000 per tonne, adding roughly ₹50 per square foot to high-rise construction costs in Mumbai, where more than 10,000 luxury units are under construction. Developers are likely to raise luxury housing prices by over 5 percent, ANAROCK said.
moneycontrol
+2

Imported Italian Statuario and Calacatta marble, widely used in Mumbai's sea-facing penthouses, now carries an additional ₹50 to ₹150 per square foot due to rerouting costs. War-risk surcharges and rerouting have added ₹2 to ₹3.5 lakh per container for cargoes linked to Gulf routes, according to the Hindustan Times. Similar pressures are building in Delhi-NCR and Bengaluru.
hindustantimes
+3

4 sources
Thailand Moves to Shield Drug Supply

Thailand's Food and Drug Administration has taken a proactive stance, fast-tracking international medicine shipments and boosting domestic production to build a six-month buffer of essential medical supplies, according to The Nation Thailand. The FDA set up a war room to monitor more than 60 critical medicines weekly and began gathering real-time stock data from over 350 operators. Pharmaceutical firms confirmed current stock levels were sufficient for three to four months, the Straits Times reported.
straitstimes
+2

Particular concern centers on drugs imported from Israel, such as the anti-coagulant warfarin, with the ministry preparing contingency plans to source alternatives from India, China, and Europe. FDA officials have also asked domestic manufacturers to temporarily halt exports and prioritize domestic supply.
nationthailand

EU grid bottlenecks put 120 GW of renewables at risk

The war in Iran is reshaping the global energy landscape at a pace few anticipated. As oil prices have surged past $100 a barrel following the U.S.-Israeli strikes launched in late February, investors, governments, and households are accelerating their pivot away from fossil fuels — a shift already well underway before the first missiles struck.

Published
3 hours ago
linkedin
China battery trio gain $70bn as Iran war sparks 'paradigm shift'
ua
Chinese battery giants gain $70 billion amid paradigm shift triggered ...
ft
China battery trio gain $70bn as Iran war sparks 'paradigm shift'
tradearabia
Near-700 GW surge in 2025 proves renewable energy resilience
reuters.com
Battery Boom and Renewable Records

China's three largest battery and energy storage companies — CATL, BYD, and Sungrow — have collectively gained more than $70 billion in market capitalization since the conflict began, outperforming global oil majors including ExxonMobil, Chevron, Shell, and BP, according to the Financial Times. CATL's China-traded shares have risen 19 percent, BYD has gained nearly 22 percent, and Sungrow is up over 19 percent since late February.
linkedin
+2

The crisis has landed atop an already record-breaking year for clean energy. The International Renewable Energy Agency reported on March 31 that global renewable power capacity grew by 692 GW in 2025, bringing the total to 5,149 GW. Solar alone accounted for 511 GW of new additions, with wind contributing 159 GW. In the European Union, wind and solar generated 30 percent of all electricity in 2025, overtaking fossil fuels at 29 percent for the first time, according to data from the energy think tank Ember published by Reuters.
tradearabia
+3

7 sources
Europe's Grid Crunch

Yet Europe's ability to capitalize on the momentum faces a structural obstacle. An Ember report highlighted by outlets including PV Tech and Euronews found that grid bottlenecks across 20 EU countries are putting more than 120 GW of planned renewable capacity at risk before 2030. In eight countries — including Austria, the Netherlands, Poland, and Portugal — available grid capacity can accommodate less than 10 percent of planned renewables. Nearly 700 GW of projects are already queued for grid connection across ten member states. IEA Executive Director Fatih Birol underscored the urgency at the World Economic Forum in January, telling Euronews that Europe's path forward is to "electrify everything" and that "it's all about grids, grids, and more grids".
news.yahoo
+3

4 sources
The Electrostate Era

Analysts argue the conflict is exposing the structural cost of fossil fuel dependence. Columbia University's Center on Global Energy Policy has framed the emerging divide as one between "petrostates" and "electrostates," noting that 70 percent of the world's population lives in fossil-fuel-importing countries now weighing a faster transition. In the UK, data from renewables firm Glow Green showed interest in solar panels surging 182 percent year-on-year as homeowners brace for higher energy bills. "If current trends continue, we could see a similar pattern emerge again where growing demand for solar panels outpaces supply," said Lloyd Greenfield, a renewables expert at the company.
theintermediary

What the Offering Includes

The Agentic Service Management package combines a maturity model, structured assessments, and implementation blueprints, delivered through Kyndryl Consult. The maturity assessment evaluates an organization's readiness across service management, AI governance, security, and operations, then produces a tailored gap analysis and phased roadmap for adopting agentic IT service management.
kyndryl

The assessments are aligned to ISO 42001 standards, helping customers review existing policies, controls, and workflows against governance frameworks for AI-native environments. Kyndryl emphasized that security and reliability serve as core design principles, with human oversight built into the autonomous capabilities.

It provides a security-first framework for managing how AI agents operate, targeting regulated industries where data protection, compliance, and classification requirements are essential. Prominent Fortnite dataminer ShiinaBR revealed on X that Buzz Lightyear and Zurg will debut as Showdown Cup skins, indicating the collaboration will use a competitive tournament format — similar to past events like The Rock versus Ice King — to give players early access before the characters hit the Item Shop. The format, referred to as the "Buzz vs. Zurg" cup, positions the two as rivals in a head-to-head event.

Police, FIFA probe anti-Muslim chants at Spain-Egypt friendly

Anti-Muslim chants by Spanish fans during a pre-World Cup friendly between Spain and Egypt on Tuesday marred what was meant to be a routine warm-up match, prompting investigations by local police and a review by FIFA that could result in sanctions against the Spanish national team.

Published
17 hours ago
espn
Spain's Lamine Yamal condemns anti-Muslim chants; police ... - ESPN
surinenglish
Spain–Egypt friendly in Barcelona marred by alleged Islamophobic ...
as
No consequences for the World Cup - AS USA - Diario AS
dw
Spain: Anti-Muslim chants mar Egypt soccer friendly
aljazeera.com
"Disrespectful and Intolerable"

The match, held at RCDE Stadium in Barcelona, ended in a 0-0 draw but was overshadowed by repeated Islamophobic chanting from sections of the crowd. Fans sang "Musulmán el que no bote" — roughly, "If you're not jumping, you're a Muslim" — during the first half, while the Egyptian national anthem was met with loud whistling before kickoff. Stadium officials displayed anti-discrimination messages on screens at halftime and again early in the second half, but the referee did not activate FIFA's anti-racism protocol.
as
+2

Spain star Lamine Yamal, an 18-year-old practicing Muslim whose father is Moroccan, posted a pointed response on Instagram. "I am Muslim, alhamdulillah," he wrote. "I know it was against the opposition and nothing personal, but as a Muslim it is still disrespectful and completely intolerable. To use religion as a way of mocking others inside a stadium is ignorant and racist".
espn

Head coach Luis de la Fuente said he felt "total and absolute disgust" toward "any form of xenophobia, racism, and disrespect".
dw
+1

5 sources
Investigations and Potential FIFA Sanctions

Catalonia's regional police force, the Mossos d'Esquadra, announced on Wednesday that it is investigating "Islamophobic and xenophobic chants" from the match in coordination with the Prosecutor's Office for Hate Crimes and Discrimination. Officers are analyzing footage and social media content to identify those responsible.
surinenglish
+1

A source told ESPN that FIFA will also analyze reports from the referee, the match inspector, and the on-site security team, with Spain facing potential sanctions ahead of the 2026 World Cup. The Egyptian Football Association called the chanting a "reprehensible racist act" and said it is working with FIFA officials to prevent future incidents. FIFA itself stated that "what happened is completely unacceptable" and reaffirmed its commitment to combating racism.
espn

3 sources
Broader Context

The incident arrives amid heightened scrutiny of racism in football. Earlier this year, Real Madrid's Vinícius Júnior alleged racist abuse from Benfica's Gianluca Prestianni during a Champions League match, leading to a UEFA investigation and provisional suspension. Berni Álvarez, Catalonia's sports minister, criticized organizers for a delayed response, saying the match "should have been stopped" after the first chant. With the World Cup approaching this summer, Spain now faces the unwelcome possibility of disciplinary action at a moment when the sport's governing bodies are under pressure to show that anti-racism protocols are more than words on paper.
aljazeera

Djokovic, Draper, Fritz all out of Monte Carlo Masters

The 2026 Rolex Monte Carlo Masters has lost several marquee names before a ball has been struck, with Novak Djokovic, Jack Draper, Taylor Fritz, and Sebastian Korda all pulling out of the ATP Masters 1000 event set to begin on April 5 at the Monte Carlo Country Club in Roquebrune-Cap-Martin, France.

Novak Djokovic withdraws from Monte-Carlo | ATP Tour | Tennis
atptour.com
Djokovic's Shoulder Woes Continue

Djokovic's withdrawal, announced by the tournament via Instagram on March 27, extends an absence that began when the 38-year-old Serb pulled out of the Miami Open in mid-March with a right shoulder injury. The 24-time Grand Slam champion last competed at Indian Wells, where he lost a three-set battle to Draper in the fourth round. His exit from Monte Carlo marks the first time in 15 years, outside of the pandemic-cancelled 2020 edition, that the two-time champion will miss the event. Djokovic, who has slipped out of the world's top three in the ATP rankings, is next scheduled to compete at the Mutua Madrid Open.
skysports
+5

6 sources
Draper Delays Clay Debut

Draper confirmed his withdrawal on Tuesday, opting to continue training rather than rush into the clay swing. According to Sky Sports, the British player plans to return to competition at the Barcelona Open, which runs from April 13 to 19. Draper endured a difficult 2025 season, missing six months of action due to a bruised humerus bone, and his camp appears determined to manage his workload carefully. He lost his opening match at the Miami Open before deciding to regroup.
skysports
+1

2 sources
Fritz, Korda Also Out

Fritz, the American ranked seventh in the world, withdrew from the tournament over a week before the start, adding to a growing list of absentees. Korda, who has dealt with recurring back issues this season, also pulled out. Despite the high-profile departures, the draw will still feature defending champion Carlos Alcaraz, world No. 1 Jannik Sinner, Alexander Zverev, and Lorenzo Musetti. The draw is scheduled to be made on Saturday, April 4, at 5 p.m. local time.

Italy miss third straight World Cup as 48-team field is set

Four-time champions Italy will miss a third consecutive FIFA World Cup after a devastating penalty shootout loss to Bosnia-Herzegovina on Tuesday, a result that filled the last remaining European berths and completed the 48-team lineup for the expanded tournament set to kick off on June 11 across the United States, Canada, and Mexico.

rte.ie
Italy's Collapse in Zenica

Italy's campaign ended in agony at Bilino Polje Stadium in Zenica, where a first-half red card to defender Alessandro Bastoni proved fatal. Moise Kean had given the Azzurri an early lead in the 15th minute, but Haris Tabakovic equalized for Bosnia in the 79th, and the match finished 1-1 after extra time. In the shootout, Italian substitutes Pio Esposito and Bryan Cristante both failed from the spot, and Esmir Bajraktarevic converted the winning penalty to seal a 4-1 shootout victory for Bosnia.
espn
+1

The defeat extends Italy's absence from football's biggest stage to 12 years. The Azzurri have not appeared at a World Cup since Brazil 2014, having failed to qualify for both the 2018 and 2022 editions. Bosnia, meanwhile, will make their second World Cup appearance when they take the field in Group B alongside Canada, Qatar, and Switzerland.

All 48 Spots Now Filled

DR Congo also qualified by seeing off Jamaica, returning to the tournament for the first time in over five decades.

The 2026 FIFA World Cup field is set. Following a night of drama on March 31 that saw Italy eliminated for a third consecutive tournament and Iraq return to the world stage for the first time in 40 years, all 48 teams are now confirmed for the expanded edition of the competition, which will run from June 11 to July 19 across 16 host cities in the United States, Canada, and Mexico.

Six Teams Clinch Final Spots

Tuesday's playoffs delivered high stakes across six simultaneous matches. Iraq secured the 48th and final berth with a 2-1 victory over Bolivia at Estadio BBVA in Monterrey, ending a World Cup absence stretching back to Mexico 1986. Iraq will slot into Group I alongside France, Senegal, and Norway, with a group-stage meeting against France scheduled for June 22 at Lincoln Financial Field in Philadelphia.

They will face co-hosts the United States, Paraguay, and Australia in Group D. Sweden edged Poland 3-2 thanks to an 88th-minute winner from Viktor Gyökeres to claim a spot in Group F. The Czech Republic beat Denmark on penalties to enter Group A, while Bosnia and Herzegovina stunned four-time champions Italy 4-1 in a shootout in Zenica, as reported by the BBC.

Turkey qualify for 2026 World Cup, ending 24-year absence

Turkey ended a 24-year World Cup drought on Tuesday, defeating Kosovo 1-0 in their UEFA playoff final in Pristina to secure a place at this summer's tournament in the United States, Mexico, and Canada. Kerem Aktürkoglu scored the only goal in the 53rd minute, redirecting a shot from Orkun Kökçü into the net at the Stadiumi Fadil Vokrri to send the Turkish national team back to soccer's biggest stage for the first time since their storied semifinal run in 2002.

beinsports.com
A Long Wait Ends

Turkey's return completes Group D at the 2026 World Cup, where they will face co-hosts the United States, along with Paraguay and Australia, with the group stage set to begin on June 12. The qualification marks only Turkey's third World Cup appearance in history, following a group-stage exit in 1954 and a third-place finish in Japan and South Korea in 2002. For Kosovo, the defeat ended their dream of a first-ever World Cup appearance.

+4

The Fenerbahçe forward Aktürkoglu proved the difference in what was a tightly contested affair. Turkey, coached by Mircea Lucescu, had also needed to fight through a difficult semifinal round to reach Tuesday's final.

Michal Sadílek converted the decisive spot kick to send Czechia to their first World Cup since 2006. Italy miss third straight World Cup after shootout loss to Bosnia

Four-time world champions Italy were eliminated from the 2026 FIFA World Cup on Tuesday after a 4-1 penalty shootout loss to Bosnia and Herzegovina in Zenica, becoming the first former World Cup winners to miss three consecutive editions of the tournament.
espn
+1

Published
Apr 1, 2026
espn
Italy miss out on 3rd-straight WC in shootout loss to Bosnia
cbssports
World Cup qualifying: Italy fail to qualify for third straight time; Turkiye to face USMNT
sportingnews
Italy red card, explained: Why Alessandro Bastoni was sent off vs ...
+37 sources
reuters.com
A Lead Squandered

Gennaro Gattuso's side took an early lead when Moise Kean capitalized on a mistake by Bosnian goalkeeper Nikola Vasilj, calmly finishing to make it 1-0 in the 15th minute at Bilino Polje Stadium. It was Kean's second goal in as many playoff matches after scoring in last week's semifinal victory over Northern Ireland.
cbssports
+1

The dynamics of the match shifted before halftime when center-back Alessandro Bastoni was shown a straight red card in the 42nd minute for a last-man tackle on Amar Memic, leaving Italy to play with 10 men for the remainder of the contest. Bosnia pressed relentlessly with the extra man, and substitute Haris Tabakovic finally broke through in the 79th minute to level the score at 1-1. Italy goalkeeper Gianluigi Donnarumma made at least four crucial saves to keep the Azzurri alive through extra time, but neither side could find a winner in the additional 30 minutes.
espn
+3

4 sources
Penalties Seal Italy's Fate

In the shootout, Italy's misery was swift. The Azzurri hit the crossbar and skied another attempt, converting just one of their four penalties, while Bosnia were flawless, scoring all four of theirs to clinch a 4-1 victory from the spot.
espn
+2

The result extends a painful era for Italian football. Italy last appeared at a World Cup in 2014 in Brazil and have not won a knockout-round match at the tournament since the 2006 final, when they beat France to lift the trophy. They were eliminated from qualifying by Sweden ahead of the 2018 tournament and by North Macedonia before the 2022 edition.
espn
+1

4 sources
Bosnia Return to the World Stage

For Bosnia and Herzegovina, the victory in Zenica ends a 12-year wait and secures their place at a second World Cup. They will join Group B alongside co-hosts Canada, Switzerland, and Qatar when the tournament kicks off in North America this summer. Bosnia had already shown their nerve in the playoff semifinal, beating Wales on penalties after a 1-1 draw in Cardiff.
bolavip
+3

FIFA confirms Iran will play World Cup games in the US as scheduled

FIFA President Gianni Infantino declared on Tuesday that Iran will compete in its 2026 World Cup group-stage matches at venues in the United States as originally scheduled, rejecting proposals to relocate the games to Mexico amid the ongoing military conflict between the US, Israel, and Iran.

"There Is Only Plan A"

We're delighted because they're a very, very strong team," he said. "The matches will be played where they are supposed to be, according to the draw."

Caster Semenya plans class action suit over IOC trans ban

The International Olympic Committee announced last Thursday that transgender women and most intersex athletes will be barred from competing in women's events at the Olympics, introducing mandatory genetic screening that marks the most sweeping eligibility change in decades. The policy, effective from the 2028 Los Angeles Games onward, limits participation in all female category events to "biological females," determined by a one-time SRY gene test.
ESPN
+1

Published
Mar 30, 2026
aljazeera
France calls IOC sex testing a 'step backwards' while Trump praises ...
africa.espn
Transgender women banned from Olympics by new IOC policy
olympics
International Olympic Committee announces new Policy on the ...
youtube
New International Olympic Committee policy bans transgender ...
news.sky.com
A Reversal Years in the Making

The IOC had long declined to set a universal rule on transgender participation, instead leaving eligibility decisions to individual sports federations. Under the new framework, athletes must undergo screening for the SRY gene, a DNA segment found on the Y chromosome that triggers male sex development. Testing can be done via saliva, cheek swab, or blood sample, and a negative result permanently satisfies the eligibility requirement. Athletes who test positive are disqualified from women's events, with narrow exceptions for those diagnosed with complete androgen insensitivity syndrome.
olympics
+1

IOC President Kirsty Coventry, the first woman to lead the organization, said the policy was "led by medical experts" and described it as protecting "fairness, safety and integrity in the female category". The 10-page policy document also restricts female athletes with differences in sex development, such as two-time Olympic 800-meter champion Caster Semenya. The IOC noted the policy "is not retroactive and does not apply to any grassroots or recreational sports programs".
ESPN
youtube
espn
+1

5 sources
Backlash and Support

The decision has drawn sharp criticism. France's sports minister Marina Ferrari called it a "step backwards," saying her government was "greatly concerned" about the broad application of genetic testing, which she said raises "ethical, legal, and medical issues". A coalition of more than 100 human rights organizations warned the testing could inflict "significant harm" on affected athletes and called it an "imprecise measure of both sex and athletic advantage".
aljazeera
+2

Semenya, speaking on Sunday, expressed disappointment with Coventry and announced she is mounting a class action lawsuit against the IOC. Legal experts have pointed to likely challenges at the Court of Arbitration for Sport and potentially the European Court of Human Rights.
thecanary
+3

7 sources
Political Dimensions

Veteran sportscaster Bob Costas voiced support for the ban, saying "common sense is not transphobic" and arguing that allowing biological males to compete in women's events would undermine fair competition. The policy aligns with a February 2025 executive order from President Donald Trump prohibiting transgender athletes from girls' and women's sports, a connection multiple outlets noted ahead of the LA Games being held on American soil. Before the 2024 Paris Olympics, track and field, swimming, and cycling had already adopted similar restrictions, but the IOC's decision now extends them across all Olympic disciplines.
cnn
+3

4 sources

Norris, Verstappen blast F1 power unit rules after Suzuka

Reigning world champion Lando Norris and four-time champion Max Verstappen continued their vocal criticism of Formula 1's 2026 power unit regulations following Sunday's Japanese Grand Prix at Suzuka, with Norris declaring that driver complaints are unlikely to prompt meaningful changes. Norris finished fifth and Verstappen eighth as Mercedes' Kimi Antonelli won his second consecutive race.

'This Is Not Racing'

Norris was blunt in his post-race assessment, describing the uncontrollable energy deployment as fundamentally contrary to racing. "Honestly some of the racing, I didn't even want to overtake Lewis. It's just that my battery deploys, I don't want it to deploy, but I can't control it," Norris told Autosport. "So, I overtake him, and then I have no battery left, so he just flies past. This is not racing, this is yo-yoing."
Autosport

The McLaren driver said drivers are powerless behind the wheel when the power unit dictates their pace. "When you're just at the mercy of whatever the power unit delivers, the driver should be in control of it at least, and we're not," he said. Norris also lamented the feel of Suzuka under the new rules, saying it "hurts the soul" to watch speeds bleed away through the circuit's famous high-speed corners.
planetf1
+1

Verstappen, who qualified only 11th and has yet to score a podium in 2026, has been the most persistent critic of the regulations since pre-season testing, when he labelled the new cars "Formula E on steroids". At Suzuka, he said he was "beyond frustrated" with the state of the sport.

Safety Fears Escalate After Bearman Crash

Grand Prix Drivers' Association director Carlos Sainz was furious, telling Sky Sports F1 that drivers had warned the FIA this would happen. "Imagine going to Baku or Singapore or Vegas and having these kind of closing speeds next to the walls," Sainz said.
gpfans

The FIA responded with a statement confirming that "a number of meetings are scheduled in April to assess the operation of the new regulations and to determine whether any refinements are required" before the Miami Grand Prix. Despite this, Norris expressed skepticism that drivers' voices would lead to real change, saying "it doesn't matter what we say".

Semenya calls IOC transgender ban 'a lie,' rips Coventry

The International Olympic Committee on Thursday announced a sweeping new policy barring transgender women from competing in women's events at the Olympics and all IOC-sanctioned competitions, effective from the 2028 Los Angeles Games. The decision, which also restricts athletes with differences in sex development, drew sharp criticism from two-time Olympic 800-meter champion Caster Semenya, who on Sunday called the ruling "a lie" and expressed deep disappointment with IOC President Kirsty Coventry.

Published
Mar 29, 2026
espn.com
Transgender women banned from Olympics by new IOC policy - ESPN
wfmd
IOC announces new policy to ensure only females compete in women’s competitions
olympics
International Olympic Committee announces new Policy on the ...
essentiallysports
Caster Semenya Harshly Slams IOC Chief Over Transgender Policy
citizen.co.za
A New Era of Genetic Testing

Under the policy, titled "Protection of the Female (Women's) Category in Olympic Sport," eligibility for any female-category event will be determined by a one-time screening for the SRY gene, found on the Y chromosome. Athletes who test positive for the gene will be barred from women's events but may compete in male, mixed, or open categories. The test can be administered via saliva, cheek swab, or blood sample.
ESPN
+2

"Eligibility for any female category event at the Olympic Games or any other IOC event, including individual and team sports, is now limited to biological females," the IOC stated in its 10-page policy document. Coventry, who was elected as the first female IOC president in June 2025, defended the decision, saying in a video statement that "it would not be fair for biological males to compete in the female category" and that the policy was "based on science and has been led by medical experts".
essentiallysports
+2

The policy also affects athletes with differences in sex development who test SRY-positive, with narrow exceptions for conditions such as complete androgen insensitivity syndrome. The IOC said the rules are not retroactive and do not apply to grassroots or recreational sports.
olympics
+1

5 sources
Semenya Fires Back

Speaking at a press conference in Cape Town on Sunday, Semenya directed her frustration squarely at Coventry, a fellow African and former Olympic swimmer from Zimbabwe. "For her being a woman coming from Africa, knowing how African women or women in the global South are affected by that, of course, it causes harm," Semenya told reporters, according to the Associated Press.
bastillepost

Semenya, who was assigned female at birth but has naturally elevated testosterone levels, has been barred from her specialist 800-meter event since 2019 after refusing to take medication to lower her hormone levels. She dismissed the IOC's scientific justification outright: "If the science is clear, show us who decided and don't dress that as a lie because it's a lie". In an exclusive Sky News interview, she called the policy "nonsense" and urged women athletes to mount a class-action challenge.
news.sky
+2

3 sources
Reaction From All Sides

American middle-distance runner Nikki Hiltz, who is transgender and nonbinary and competed at the 2024 Paris Olympics, wrote on Instagram that the policy "is so f---ing stupid and not solving a problem that exists," noting that no transgender women competed in Paris. France's Sports Minister Marina Ferrari called the return to genetic testing "a step backwards" that raises "ethical, legal, and medical questions".
sports.yahoo
+3

The White House, meanwhile, celebrated the decision. Press Secretary Karoline Leavitt credited President Donald Trump's executive order on women's sports, writing on X: "President Trump's Executive Order protecting women's sports made this happen!" The IOC made no reference to the U.S. president in its announcement.

Ukraine asks IOC to reexamine Russian athletes' neutral status

Ukrainian sports authorities on Wednesday formally asked the International Olympic Committee to reexamine the "neutral" status granted to Russian athletes, presenting evidence they say shows direct ties between some competitors and Russian military structures.

The appeal, signed by Ukrainian Sports Minister Matvii Bidny and National Olympic Committee head Vadym Guttsait, accuses certain athletes of flouting eligibility rules the IOC established in 2023, more than a year after Russia's full-scale invasion of Ukraine. Athletes from Russia and Belarus were permitted to compete at the 2024 Paris Olympics and the 2026 Milano Cortina Winter Games only as Individual Neutral Athletes, subject to vetting that barred anyone linked to the military or found to have supported the invasion.
apnews
+2

Published

Freedom of Expression at the Olympic Games – The case of…
aljazeera.com
Military Ties and a Moscow Competition

The Ukrainian appeal cited what it called "systematic violations" in sports climbing and its governing body, the International Federation of Sport Climbing. "The Ukrainian side has provided evidence of direct links between a number of athletes and the military structures of the aggressor state," the statement said, according to a Reuters report carried by CNA. It named several athletes the officials alleged had links to the military, supported the invasion, or had trained in Russian-occupied Crimea.
channelnewsasia

The appeal also flagged an international competition held in Moscow last November under the auspices of the International Military Sports Council, which Ukraine said violated IOC rules barring sports events in Russia. "This confirms the involvement of Russian military structures in the international sports movement with the aim of legitimising Russia's aggressive policy," the appeal stated.
channelnewsasia

Ukraine called on the IOC and the IFSC "to conduct a comprehensive review of these facts and to suspend the individuals in question from international competitions".
channelnewsasia

1 source
Heraskevych Vows to Fight On

Separately, Ukrainian skeleton pilot Vladyslav Heraskevych, who was barred from competing at the Milano Cortina Games in February for refusing to remove a helmet bearing images of Ukrainian athletes killed in Russia's invasion, said he intends to take his case to a human rights court.
sportnation
+1

Speaking on The Ariel Helwani Show on Tuesday, Heraskevych described the Court of Arbitration for Sport proceedings that upheld his disqualification as "a mockery," saying he was "suspended because of intention to violate the rules" rather than any actual violation. CAS had dismissed his appeal on February 13, ruling that the IOC's expression guidelines struck a fair balance between athletes' rights and the committee's aim to keep the field of play free from political expression.
bratschi
+2

The IOC had offered Heraskevych the option of wearing a black armband instead, which he rejected. He was allowed to keep his accreditation and remain at the Games but never competed. The controversy drew support from prominent Ukrainian athletes, including boxers Oleksandr Usyk and the Klitschko brothers.
olympics
+1

The twin challenges underscore the deepening friction between Ukraine and the IOC over the terms of Russian participation in international sport, even as some governing bodies have begun easing restrictions on athletes from Russia and Belarus.

Italy miss third straight World Cup after shootout loss to Bosnia

Four-time world champions Italy were eliminated from the 2026 FIFA World Cup on Tuesday after a 4-1 penalty shootout loss to Bosnia and Herzegovina in Zenica, becoming the first former World Cup winners to miss three consecutive editions of the tournament.
espn
+1

Published
Apr 1, 2026

reuters.com
A Lead Squandered

Gennaro Gattuso's side took an early lead when Moise Kean capitalized on a mistake by Bosnian goalkeeper Nikola Vasilj, calmly finishing to make it 1-0 in the 15th minute at Bilino Polje Stadium. It was Kean's second goal in as many playoff matches after scoring in last week's semifinal victory over Northern Ireland.
cbssports
+1

The dynamics of the match shifted before halftime when center-back Alessandro Bastoni was shown a straight red card in the 42nd minute for a last-man tackle on Amar Memic, leaving Italy to play with 10 men for the remainder of the contest. Bosnia pressed relentlessly with the extra man, and substitute Haris Tabakovic finally broke through in the 79th minute to level the score at 1-1. Italy goalkeeper Gianluigi Donnarumma made at least four crucial saves to keep the Azzurri alive through extra time, but neither side could find a winner in the additional 30 minutes.
espn
+3

4 sources
Penalties Seal Italy's Fate

In the shootout, Italy's misery was swift. The Azzurri hit the crossbar and skied another attempt, converting just one of their four penalties, while Bosnia were flawless, scoring all four of theirs to clinch a 4-1 victory from the spot.
espn
+2

The result extends a painful era for Italian football. Italy last appeared at a World Cup in 2014 in Brazil and have not won a knockout-round match at the tournament since the 2006 final, when they beat France to lift the trophy. They were eliminated from qualifying by Sweden ahead of the 2018 tournament and by North Macedonia before the 2022 edition.

Bosnia had already shown their nerve in the playoff semifinal, beating Wales on penalties after a 1-1 draw in Cardiff.

Tom Pidcock withdraws from Volta a Catalunya after ravine crash

Tom Pidcock's 2026 Volta a Catalunya came to an abrupt end on Saturday when the British rider was forced to withdraw before Stage 6, a day after a harrowing crash sent him tumbling into a ravine during the descent of the Collada Sobirana on Stage 5.
cyclingnews
+1

The Pinarello-Q36.5 rider, who had been sitting second overall after a strong opening week, misjudged a corner while drinking from his bottle with roughly 30 kilometres remaining on Friday's queen stage from La Seu d'Urgell to Coll de Pal. He overshot the turn and plunged off the road and out of sight of the race convoy.
cyclinguptodate
+1

Mar 28, 2026

'Today I Lost a Life for Sure'

cyclinguptodate
+1

The severity of the incident was compounded by the fact that nobody initially knew where Pidcock was. "I am lucky I could talk on the radio. I was far from the road, and nobody knew I was there," he explained. The 26-year-old, fresh off a second-place finish at Milan-San Remo, managed to climb back to the road, change bikes, and finish the stage — albeit nearly half an hour behind the leaders, dropping to 74th overall.
cyclinguptodate
+1

On Saturday morning, the team confirmed the withdrawal. "We did everything to try to make it to the start but it's not possible," Pidcock said. Team doctor Lorenz Emmert detailed the injuries: "He suffered injuries, most likely bone and ligament damage in particular to his right knee and also right wrist." Fractures have been ruled out, but further imaging is planned in the coming days, casting doubt over his Ardennes Classics campaign.

screenrant

"I would be thrilled to do Luigi's Mansion, just because it's such a fun game," Day said. "And not that you would make it like a horror movie for kids, but it could have some more sort of jump scares in it, which would be fun."

Jack Black hints third Super Mario movie is coming in 2029

Jack Black appears to have let slip that a third Super Mario movie is already in development, casually dropping a potential 2029 release window during a press interview ahead of The Super Mario Galaxy Movie, which opens in theaters on April 1.

A Bowser-Sized Slip of the Tongue

dexerto
+1

The first two films were released three years apart — The Super Mario Bros. Movie debuted in April 2023 and The Super Mario Galaxy Movie follows in April 2026 — making 2029 a logical next step.

An Expanding Nintendo Cinematic Universe

Nintendo president Shuntaro Furukawa announced plans in late 2025 to maintain a "consistent release cadence" of feature films, and a live-action Legend of Zelda movie directed by Wes Ball is slated for 2027. A standalone Donkey Kong film is also reportedly in development.

+1

Celine Dion announces 10-show Paris residency in concert comeback

Celine Dion confirmed her return to the concert stage on Monday, her 58th birthday, announcing a 10-night residency at the Paris La Défense Arena running from September 12 through October 14. The announcement, delivered through an emotional video posted to her Instagram account, caps weeks of mounting speculation fueled by a cryptic poster campaign across the French capital.
purewow
+1

Published
Mar 30, 2026
purewow
Céline Dion Makes Major Announcement—and Fans Are Freaking Out
sortiraparis
Could Celine Dion be returning to perform at Paris La Défense ...
ew
Celine Dion sets concert comeback 4 years after stiff-person ...
instagram
CELINE DION PARIS 2026 10 unforgettable shows starting this ...
ew.com
"The Best Gift of My Life"

"I want to let you know that I'm doing great. Managing my health, feeling good. I'm singing again, even doing a little bit of dancing," Dion told fans in the video. "This year, I'm getting the best gift of my life. I'm getting the chance to see you, to perform for you once again, in Paris. I'm so happy. I'm so ready to do this. I'm feeling good. I'm strong; I'm feeling excited."
purewow

The residency will feature two performances per week at Europe's largest indoor concert venue, which seats up to 40,000 spectators. Specific dates include September 12, 16, 19, 23, 26, and 30, followed by October 3, 7, 10, and 14. Artist presale registration opens through April 2 at CelineDion.com, with presale tickets available starting April 7.
sortiraparis
+4

5 sources
A Long Road Back

The Paris shows will mark Dion's first major concert series since March 8, 2020, when she wrapped the North American leg of her Courage World Tour in Newark, New Jersey. That tour's European dates were first postponed due to the pandemic, then shelved indefinitely after Dion revealed in December 2022 that she had been diagnosed with Stiff Person Syndrome, a rare neurological condition affecting roughly one or two people per million.
today
+2

The disease causes debilitating muscle stiffness and spasms, particularly impacting the muscles used for singing. Dion's treatment has included intravenous immunoglobulin therapy, vocal rehabilitation, and physical therapy. Her 2024 Prime Video documentary, "I Am: Celine Dion," offered an unflinching look at the toll the condition has taken on her daily life.
patientworthy
+2

4 sources
Building Momentum

Dion's path back to performing began publicly at the Paris 2024 Olympics opening ceremony, where she delivered a performance of Edith Piaf's "Hymne à l'amour" from the Eiffel Tower — her first live appearance in over four years. The buzz around her full comeback intensified on March 23, when posters referencing her iconic songs, including "My Heart Will Go On" and "Power of Love," appeared on streets across Paris. French outlet BFMTV captured the Eiffel Tower lit with the message "Céline Dion, Paris, Je Suis Prête" — "I'm Ready". The 10-date schedule represents a deliberately scaled-back approach compared to the original 52-date Courage World Tour, reflecting the careful management of her condition.

## TÍTULO: [Perplexity]
**Fecha:** [Unknown] | **URL:** [https://www.perplexity.ai/discover/entertainment/global-streaming-subscription-L4wm7Q7ISTy5ft9e24N3HA]

### Contenido Principal
Back to Discover
Share
Global streaming subscription revenue hit $157B in 2025, Ampere says

Global streaming subscription revenue surpassed $150 billion for the first time in 2025, reaching a record $157.1 billion — a 14% year-over-year increase that marks a tripling of the $50 billion recorded during the pandemic year of 2020, according to new research from Ampere Analysis published Sunday.
mediaplaynews
+1

The findings underscore a streaming industry that has shifted from a growth-at-all-costs subscriber race to a maturing business focused on wringing more revenue from existing audiences through price hikes and ad-supported plans.

Published
Mar 30, 2026
mediaplaynews
Ampere: Global Subscription Streaming Video Revenue Topped ...
deadline
Global Streaming Subscription Revenue To Hit $200 Billion By 2030 ...
todotvnews
Ampere Analysis: Global Streaming Revenue Exceeds $150 billion
variety
U.S. Streaming Video Market to Surge 33% by 2029 to Over $112B
variety.com
The U.S. and Netflix Lead the Way

The United States remains the engine of the global streaming economy, accounting for 50% of worldwide subscription revenue in 2025. Netflix is the single largest contributor to the U.S. market, with its revenue rising 14% in 2025 after the company implemented across-the-board price increases at the start of that year.
deadline
+1

Ampere forecasts that subscription revenue will grow a further 29% over the next five years, surpassing $200 billion globally by 2030. When advertising revenue is included, streaming services generated $177 billion worldwide in 2025, with advertising expected to add another $42 billion in annual revenue by 2030.
mediaplaynews
+1

2 sources
Ad-Supported Tiers Reshape the Business

Perhaps the most striking structural change in the industry is the rapid rise of ad-supported subscription tiers. Their share of total streaming subscription revenue climbed from less than 5% in 2020 to 28% in 2025, according to Ampere. In mature, crowded markets such as North America and Western Europe, these hybrid subscription-and-advertising models have become the primary engine of the next phase of expansion.
todotvnews
+2

"As the streaming market matures, the emphasis is no longer on pure subscriber growth but on extracting greater value from existing audiences," said Lauren Liversedge, senior analyst at Ampere Analysis. "Price optimization and the rise of ad-supported tiers are driving revenue growth, particularly in the most competitive markets."
mediaplaynews

3 sources
A Broader Industry Shift

The Ampere data fits within a wider consensus that streaming has entered a new era. Separate research from Omdia last year projected global video streaming revenue of $214.6 billion in 2025 when including all online video categories, with advertising revenue from the five largest U.S. subscription services expected to reach $24.3 billion by 2030. PwC has similarly forecast the U.S. streaming market alone will exceed $112 billion by 2029.
variety
+1

The question now is how long price increases and ad-tier adoption can sustain double-digit growth before consumer resistance sets in — a tension Ampere's own projections implicitly acknowledge by forecasting a slower 29% gain over the next five years compared with the tripling achieved in the last five.

2 sources
Discover more
Short drama apps rank among fastest-growing subscription categories globally
The report also highlights a divergence in how short drama and traditional streaming apps are monetized. Short drama apps rank among fastest-growing subscription categories globally

AppsFlyer released its State of Subscriptions for Marketers 2026 report on Tuesday, revealing that short-form serialized video apps — commonly known as "short drama" or "microdrama" apps — have become one of the fastest-growing subscription categories in the global app economy. The report finds that aggressive marketing spend has driven Android downloads of short drama apps up 42% year-over-year, with India alone seeing a 423% surge in paid installs.
androidpolice

The findings arrive as the microdrama format, built around bite-sized vertical video clips originally designed for platforms like TikTok and Instagram Reels, has matured into a standalone app category led by players such as DramaBox and ReelShort. According to Sensor Tower's separate State of Mobile 2026 report, the category generated $2.98 billion in in-app revenue in 2025, a 115% year-over-year increase, making it the third-highest revenue growth category across all mobile apps.
marketingdive

Published
androidpolice
A fast-growing trend is having a big impact on Android entertainment ...
advanced-television
Advanced Television | Digital Media Delivery
tubefilter
Microdrama apps are getting more engagement than streaming ...
marketingdive
Microdrama apps stand out on mobile: Here's what the numbers say
ciw.news
Emerging Markets Drive the Boom

The growth is far from uniform. While India and Latin America are driving the bulk of new subscribers, the appetite in North America appears to be cooling. AppsFlyer's data shows paid installs for short drama apps dropped 40% in North America last year, even as streaming app downloads in the U.S. climbed 157% over the same period. Germany, Turkey, and Mexico are among the markets showing the strongest gains at the country level, according to the report.
advanced-television
+1

The shift reflects a broader trend reshaping the app economy: Android paid installs now make up the majority of all Android installs for subscription apps, driven by a wave of new paying consumers in emerging markets. Companies are spending four times as much promoting subscription apps on Android as on iOS, according to the AppsFlyer data.
androidpolice

2 sources
A New Monetization Playbook

The report also highlights a divergence in how short drama and traditional streaming apps are monetized. Subscription-only revenue's share of streaming apps like Netflix and Disney+ has grown from 53% to 62%, while short drama apps are moving in the opposite direction, with ad-supported revenue rising to 7.4% of total revenue.
androidpolice

Research from Omdia underscores the category's engagement power. ReelShort users in the U.S. spend an average of 35.7 minutes per day on the app, compared to 24.8 minutes for Netflix and 26.9 minutes for Prime Video, according to data reported by Tubefilter. "Microdramas are no longer a niche experiment," said Maria Rua Aguete, Omdia's Head of Media and Entertainment. "They are becoming a core driver of mobile video engagement".
tubefilter

Total spend on subscription app marketing rose 24% in 2025, with short drama and streaming together accounting for much of that growth.
androidpolice

Reddit bans Paul McCartney after he shares concert photos

Paul McCartney's Reddit account was banned over the weekend after the 83-year-old former Beatle shared a Dropbox link containing photos and videos from his phone-free concert at the Fonda Theatre in Hollywood, prompting bewilderment and mockery across social media.

McCartney had posted the content to his own subreddit, r/PaulMcCartney, on Saturday, making it only his second-ever post on the platform. The gesture was meant to give fans lasting memories from his intimate March 27 show, since audience members had their phones locked in Yondr pouches throughout the performance and were unable to record it themselves. But Reddit's automated moderation systems quickly flagged the account and issued a ban, rendering his profile page inaccessible.

McCartney delivered a 23-song set on the opening night, opening with "Help!" and closing with the Abbey Road medley of "Golden Slumbers," "Carry That Weight," and "The End".

Paul McCartney announces new solo album, his first in over five years

Paul McCartney announced on Thursday his first solo album in more than five years, a deeply personal 14-track collection titled "The Boys of Dungeon Lane," set for release on May 29 through MPL/Capitol Records. The 83-year-old former Beatle simultaneously released the album's lead single, "Days We Left Behind," a spare, guitar-driven meditation on his Liverpool childhood.
hotpress
+2

Published
Mar 26, 2026
theguardian
Paul McCartney announces 18th solo album, The Boys of Dungeon Lane, promising introspection and revelation
musicradar
“While playing around on the guitar during the meeting, Paul ...
hotpress
Paul McCartney releases new single 'Days We Left Behind' ahead of ...
showbiz411
Paul McCartney's New Album Is Produced by Andrew Watt, Who ...
rollingstone.com
A Memory Song From Speke

The album draws its name from Dungeon Lane, a road near the Speke neighborhood where McCartney grew up, and the lead single serves as its emotional anchor. "This is very much a memory song for me," McCartney said in a statement. "I was thinking just that, about the days I left behind and I do often wonder if I'm just writing about the past but then I think: how can you write about anything else? It's just a lot of memories of Liverpool".
musicradar
+1

The track includes a striking passage referencing John Lennon: "We met at Forthlin Road, and wrote a secret code, to never be spoken. I stand by what I said, the promise that I made, will never be broken". McCartney described the song as touching on Lennon and the street where he grew up, with Dungeon Lane situated nearby in the working-class area of Speke.
hotpress
+2

3 sources
Born From an Unfamiliar Chord

The album's origins trace back five years to a meeting between McCartney and producer Andrew Watt, known for his work revitalizing legacy acts including the Rolling Stones and Elton John. While idly playing guitar over tea, McCartney stumbled upon a chord he did not recognize. He kept experimenting, changing one note then another, until he had a three-chord sequence that Watt suggested they record. That session produced the album's opening track, "As You Lie There".
showbiz411
+2

Recording continued during breaks in McCartney's five-year world tour, with sessions split between studios in Los Angeles and Sussex. In keeping with the spirit of his McCartney trilogy, he played the majority of instruments himself across the 14 tracks, which span what the press materials describe as "Wings-style rock, Beatles-style harmonies, McCartney-style grooves, understated intimacy, melody-driven storytelling and character songs".
musicradar
+1

4 sources
The Story Before the Story

The album is billed as McCartney's most introspective work, exploring his post-war upbringing, the resilience of his parents, and early adventures shared with George Harrison and Lennon before the world had heard of Beatlemania. "Paul revisits these not as legends or folklore but as his personal memories," the press release states. The announcement follows teaser posters that appeared across Liverpool on Tuesday, spotted and shared by McCartney's brother Mike McGear McCartney, whose son Josh designed the artwork.
ad-hoc-news
+2

"The Boys of Dungeon Lane" follows McCartney III, released in December 2020, and arrives as McCartney prepares for a broader 2026 that includes the documentary "Man on the Run" and Sam Mendes's forthcoming four-film Beatles cinematic project.
showbiz411
+1
